What is the fourth good and lawfull means that a man is to procure, and to vse, according to his abilitie and power, helpefull and profitable for the continuance of the health and strength of his body, and for the preuenting of sicknesse and weakenesse of body; and for the recouery of the health and strength of his body when they are impayred? Answ. This; honest and lawfull exercise, mouing and stirring of his body,oh. 10.23. Sam: 1.18 en. 27.3. and that seasonably and in fit time and place, and without iust offence of any; and more or lesse as the state of his body requires, and as his calling will suffer him; as walking, running, leaping, shooting, tenis-playing, hunting, and the like. Quest. What are the things that tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the body of another, or others, and to the welfare and safety of the body of another or others? Ans. They are either things inward in the heart, or out∣ward things. Quest. What are the things inward in the heart that tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the body of ano∣ther or others? Answ. Foure especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; a kinde and louing disposition and affection of heart,Ephes. 4.32. Galat. 5.22. Coloss. 3.12. kinde heartednesse towards all, whereby men or women are tractable and easie to be vsed, and to be imploy∣ed for the good of others whatsoeuer they be, in any thing wherein they may doe them good as occasion is offered; without hurt or wrong to themselues or others.
Quest. What is the second thing inward in the heart, that tends to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the body of another or others, and to the welfare and safetie of the body of another or others? Answ. This; such a meeke and calme disposition of heart,Eccles. 7.11. Mat. 11.29. Ephes. 4.2. Gala. 5.23. Coloss. 3.12. 1 Pet. 3.4. as is neither prone to prouoke, nor easily prouoked to anger by iniuries and wrongs offered or done, when men are of quiet and meeke spirits when iniuries are offered or done to them. Quest. What is the highest degree of meekenesse and quiet∣nesse of heart, in regard of iniuries and wrongs offered or done to men? Answ. Long suffering; which is,Nom. 12.3. Pro. 14.29. Pro. 15.18. 1 Cor. 13.4. Gal. 5.22. Coloss. 3.12 when men or women be∣ing much and often prouoked by iniurious words or deeds, doe notwithstanding quietly passe them ouer, and put them vp, and are still quiet and calme, and not prouoked to anger. Quest. Wherein is meekenes and long suffering to be expressed? Answ In two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; in a quiet bearing with the infirmities and frailties of others, as hastinesse, slownesse, importunitie, rash∣nesse, and with passions and perturbations appearing in their actions, so farre forth as they are troublesome, and grieuous, and displeasing to vs:Galat. 5.2. Ephes. 4.2. Coloss. 3.13. not bearing with open offences and sinnes of men, but admonishing and reprouing for such sins, keeping within the compasse of our calling. Quest. What is the second thing wherein meekenesse and long suffering is to be expressed? Answ. This; in a free remission of reuenge,Mat. 6.12. Ephes. 4.32, Coloss. 3.13 neither car∣rying in our hearts any purpose of reuenge for wrongs done to vs, or supposed to bee done, nor returning punishment and euill for euill, in way of requittal for them. Quest. VVhat is the third thing inward in the heart, that tends to the maintenance, and preseruation of the life of the body of another or others, and to the welfare and safetie of the body of a∣nother or others? Answ. This; an inward fellow-felling of that which be∣fals
others in respect of their bodies and outward estates,om. 12.15. Cor. 12.25.26▪ when men are inwardly touched and affected according to the knowne outward estate and condition of others. Quest. How are men inwardly fellow-feeling touched and af∣fected according to the knowne outward estate and condition of o∣thers? Answ. Two wayes. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Psal. 35.27. Luk. 1.58. Philip. 1.26.Answ. This; by reioycing with others that haue iust cause of reioycing for their outward good and prosperitie seene or heard of: not in respect of their ill-gotten goods, in prospering in knowne sinne. Quest. What is the second way by which men are inwardly fel∣low-feeling, touched and affected, according to the knowne outward estate and condition of others? Answ. This; by mourning and greeuing with others that haue iust cause of heauinesse: mourning▪ and griefe for the outward euill, distresse, and aduersitie seene or heard of, and by pitying them,Psal. 35.13.14. Ephes. 4.32. Coloss. 3.12. Heb. 13.3. 1 Pet. 3.8. and by being tender hearted towards them: not with such as sorrow when they ought to reioyce, nor pi∣tying men or women in respect of deserued misery, and iust punishment brought on themselues. Quest. What is the fourth thing inward in the heart, that tends to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the body of another or others, and to the welfare and safetie of the body of another or others? Rom. 12.18. Galat. 5.22. Coloss. 3.15. 1 Thess. 4.11.Answ. This; an heart disposed to peace and quietnesse, and a care and desire to maintaine concord and good agree∣ment amongst men, as much as is possible and in our power. Quest. VVherein is an heart disposed to peace and quietnesse, and a care and desire to maintaine peace and good agreement a∣mongst men, to bee expressed? Answ. In three things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Pro. 17.14. Pro: 19.11. Pro. 20.3. Iam. 3.17. Gen. 13 8.9. Math. 17.27.Answ. This; in passing by offences so farre as they con∣cerne vs in particular, and may be passed ouer without hurt or wrong to our selues or others; and sometimes for quietnes sake, in parting from our owne right.
Quest. What is the second thing wherein an heart disposed to peace and quietnesse, and a care and desire to maintaine peace, concord, and good agreement amongst men, is to be expressed? Answ. This; in construing things in the best sense,2 Sam. 10.3. 1 Cor. 13.5. and taking euery thing, if it be possible, in the best part. Quest. What is the third thing wherein an heart disposed to peace and quietnes, and a care and desire to maintaine concord and good agreement amongst men, is to be expressed? Answ. In medling onely with our owne matters and bu∣sinesses,1. Thes. 4.11. 1 Pet. 4.15. and such things as concerne vs in regard of our cal∣lings and conditions of life. Now to the outward things that tend to the mainte∣nance of the life of the body of another or others. Quest. VVhat are the outward things that tend to the main∣tenance and preseruation of the life of the body of another or o∣thers, and to the welfare and safetie of the body of another or o∣thers? Answ. They are of two sorts: either such as serue to avert and to turne away euill, wrong, hurt, or danger from the body of another or others, or such as serue for the good, helpe and comfort of the body of another or others. Quest. What are the outward things that serue to avert and to turne away euill, wrong, hurt, or danger from the body of ano∣ther or others? Answ. They are either in speech, or in action: in word, or in act or deed. Quest. What are the outward things in speech or in word that serue to avert and to turne away euill, wrong, hurt or danger from the body of another or others? Answ. Such words and speeches vttered and spoken as are for the defence and helpe of innocent persons that are help∣lesse, being either vnder the hands of oppressors,Pro: 12.6 Pro: 24.11.12▪ or followed by oppressors seeking to hurt and to wrong them either in their bodies or liues. Men are, as they are able, and accor∣ding to their place and calling, to open their mouthes, and to speake for the defence and helpe of them that are knowne to them to bee oppressed in their bodies or liues, being innocent and helplesse, especially being such as they are
bound to by some neere and speciall bond. Quest. How are men to speake for the defence and helpe of such as are knowne to them to be wronged and oppressed in their bodies or liues, being innocent and harmelesse persons, and helpe∣lesse? Answ. Three wayes. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; by speaking for them as they are able, and according to their place and calling,en: 37, 21.22. Sam: 20.32. Hest. 7.3.4.5.6. in priuate to the face of their oppressor or oppressors, to disswade him or them from offering or doing wrong vnto them in respect of their body or liues. Thus did Reuben, Gen. 37.21, 22. Thus did Ionathan, 1 Sam. 20.32. Hest. 7.3, 4, 5, 6. Quest. What is the second way by which men are to speake for the defence and helpe of such as are knowne to them to be wronged and oppressed in their bodies or liues, being innocent and harmelesse persons, and helplesse? Hest. 4.8. Iob. 29.12 to 19. Pro. 31.8.9. Iere. 38.7.8.9 Luk. 23.13.14. to 22.Answ. This; by speaking and pleading for them as they are able, and according to their place and calling, either as Witnesses, or as Aduocates, or as Iudges publikely in some open Court, for the freeing of them from wrong done or of∣fered to be done to them in respect of their bodies or liues, especially they being poore fatherlesse, widowes, or strāgers, or being religious, and yet such as either cannot or dare not plead for themselues. Quest. What is the third way by which men are to speake for the defence and helpe of such, as are knowne to them to be wronged and oppressed in their bodies or liues, being innocent and harmeles persons, and helplesse? Act. 12.4.5. Rom. 15.30.31 2 Thess. 3.1.2Answ. This; by speaking for them as they are able to God in prayer, by commending their case to the Lord, and calling on him in prayer for their succour and reliefe. Quest. What are the outward things in act or deed that serue to avert and to turne away euill, wrong, hurt or danger from the body of another or others? Answ. Such acts and deeds done, as are for the helpe and succour of innocent persons that are helplesse, being either vnder oppression and wrong, or pursued by oppressors, see∣king
to hurt and wrong them in their bodies or liues. Men are, as they are able,Exod. 2.17.18.19. Iudg. 2.10 Iudg. 3.9.15.31 and according to their place and cal∣ling, to doe such things as serue▪ for the helpe and succour of innocent persons that are helplesse, especially of such as they are bound to by some speciall relatiō, against the known euils and wrongs either already done to them, or in doing or in∣tended to be done to them in respect of their bodies or liues. Quest. What are men to doe for the helpe and succour of in∣nocent persons that are helplesse, especially to such hauing knowne euils and wrongs already done to them, and being vnder op∣pression and wrong in respect of their bodies or liues? Answ. They are as they are able, and according to their place and calling,Iob 29.12.17 Prou. 24.11. to vse their power and strength for the re∣scuing and deliuering them from vnder their oppressions and wrongs. Thus did Abraham, Gen. 14.14.15.16 Thus Dauid 1 Sam. 30.17, 18. Quest. What are men to doe for the helpe and succour of inno∣cent persons that are helplesse, especially of such as they are bound to by some neere and speciall bond, when knowne euils and wrongs are in doing, or intended to bee done to them in their bodies or liues? Answ. They are then, as they are able, to interpose their power and strength to defend and to saue them from those e∣uils and wrongs, either as they be priuate persons, or as they be Magistrates. Quest. How are men as they bee priuate persons to interpose their power and strength, to defend and to saue innocent persons that are helplesse, especially such as they are bound to by some neere and speciall bond, from knowne euills and wrongs that are in doing or intended to bee done to them in their bod es or liues? Answ. Thus; by vsing their hands, their purses,Iosh. 2.4.6. 1. Kings 18.4. their paines so farre as they are able, to protect and to saue them from vi∣olence or spoyle, especially when violence or spoyle intended is sudden, and the Magistrate absent, and it is dangerous to stay for his comming. Quest. How frre are priuate persons to interpose their po∣wer and strength to defend and to saue innocent persons that are helplesse, especially such as they are bound vnto by some neere and
speciall bond, from knowne euils and wrongs that are in doing or in∣tended to be done to them in their bodies or liues? Sam. 21.15.6.17. om. 16.4.  Iohn. 3.16.Answ. Sometimes to the hazard and aduenturing their owne liues; as when it is to the defending and sauing of the bodies and liues of such as are speciall instruments of Gods glory, and of common good, either in the Church or Com∣mon wealth. Quest. How are men as they bee Magistrates to interpose their power and strength to defend, and to saue innocent per∣sons that are helplesse, especially such as they are bound to by some neere and speciall bond, from knowne euills and wrongs that are in doing, or intended to bee done to them in their bodies or liues? Exod. 18.21. Rom. 13.4. Exod. 2.11.12 Act. 7.24.Answ. Thus; by drawing out, and vsing the sword, ac∣cording to their place and power to protect and to saue them from violence or hurt, whether it bee in doing or intended to bee done, either to their owne Subiects or For∣reiners. Now to the outward things that serue for the good, helpe, and comfort of the body of another or o∣thers. Quest. VVhat are the outward things that serue for the good, helpe, and comfort of the body of another or others? Answ. They are also either in speech or in action: in word, or in act and deed. Quest. VVhat are the outward things in speech or in word, that serue for the good, helpe and comfort of the body of another or others? Tit. 2.3. 1 Pet. 3.16.Answ. Such words and speeches vttered and spoken, as do expresse meeknesse, gentlenesse, kindnesse and loue to those to whom they are vttered and spoken. Quest. What are the words and speeches wherein men are to expresse meeknesse, gentlenesse, kindnesse and loue to those to whom they are vttered and spoken. Answ. They are of three sorts especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; Their salutations: when men meet with others, they are to salute them, being their equalls or inferiours by
their names or surnames:Ioh. 1.38. Ioh. 20.16. Iudg. 6.12. Ruth. 2.4. Luk. 1 28. Luk. 10.5. Iohn. 20.19. and to salute their Superiours by names of Honour or Office, giuing them such Titles of reuerence as belong to them, wishing them good health, prosperitie, or good successe, and the like, as occasion is offered. 2 Kings 4.29. If thou meete any salute him not; and so Christ bad his disciples Salute no man by the way: Luke 10.4. There∣fore it may seeme vnlawfull to salute others when we meete with them. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the intent of those places is not to forbid men to salute others, but that Gehazi and the Disciples should onely for that time omit the practice of the duties of com∣mon courtesie, so farre as they might hinder or delay the performance of waightier matters. Ioh. Epist. 2. vers. 10. If there come any vnto you, and bring not this doctrine, receiue him not to house, neither bid him God speed: therefore it seemes not lawfull to salute others. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; the meaning of that place is not to forbid common courtesie of man to man, but acquaintance and familiarity with Heretikes, especially such acquain∣tance and familiaritie as may seeme to giue allowance and approbation to their wicked courses, as appeares Romanes 16.17. Quest. What is the second sort of words and speeches wherin men are to expresse meeknes, gentlenes, kindnes, and loue to those to whom they are vttered and spoken? Answ. This; their answeres:Iudg. 8.2.3. 1 Sam 25.10.11.12.13. Pro. 15.1. 2 King. 18.36. 1 Sam. 1.15. men are to giue to others soft answeres, such as may neither kindle nor increase anger in them; and when they are rayled on, they are not to rayle a∣gaine; and when they are hardly spoken of, they are either to bee silent, or onely to make a iust and manifest defence of their owne innocency. Dan. 6.21.22. Joh. 8.48.49. 1 Pet. 3.9. Quest. What is the third sort of words and speeches wherein men are to expresse meeknes, gentlenes, kindnes, and loue to those to whom they are vttered or spoken? Ans. This; their admonitions & iust reproofs: when men do
admonish or iustly reproue their brethren for their faults committed of ignorance,Gen. 13.8. Galat. 6.1. or of frailtie. Quest. What are the outward things in act or deed that serue for the good, helpe, and comfort of the body of another or others? Answ. They are either in countenance and in some ge∣sture and carriage of the body, or they bee other acts and deeds. Quest. What are the outward things in countenance, and in some gesture and cariage of the body that serue for the good, helpe, and comfort of another or others? Gen. 31.2.5. Gen. 33.10. 1 Sam. 25.17 Prou. 16.15. Gen. 23.7.12Answ. All such lookes, and all such gestures of the body as doe expresse meeknesse, gentlenesse, kindnesse and loue to another or others, without dissimulation, as looking on an other with an amiable and cheerfull countenance, shewing a mans selfe affable, easie to be spoken to, and to admit talke or conference with others, as occasion is offered, or to heare an∣other or others, either in complaint or suite; bending and bowing of the body in an humble and courteous manner. Quest. VVhat are the other outward acts and deedes that serue for the good, helpe, and comfort of the bodie of another or others? Answ. They are of two sorts. Quest. What is the first of those? Gen. 14.18. 2 Sam. 10.28 31. 1 King. 10.10.13. Ier. 40.5. Acts 20.38Ans. Such acts and deeds done as doe expresse kindnesse and loue to those to whom they are done, and are for the con∣tinuance of the health, welfare, comfort, and good estate of the body of another or others; as bestowing of gifts, bene∣fits, and good turnes on others, sending of gifts and pre∣sents to them, accompanying them in their iourneyes, and the like. Quest. VVhat is the second sort of outward acts and deeds, that serue for the good helpe and comfort of the body of another or others? Answ. Such acts and deeds done as doe expresse kind∣nesse,Iob 31.16.17.18.19.20.21. Prou. 21.13. Prou. 31.20. and loue, and tender affection to those to whom they are done, and are for the relieuing of another or others be∣ing in any knowne want and distresse of body. Men are as
they are able, and as they haue power and meanes,Isai. 58.7. Math. 25.35.36.41.43. to reach out their helping hands for the reliefe of such as ought to be relieued, being any way distressed in their bodies, and known to them, either by sight or by hearing to stand in need of re∣liefe, in respect of their bodies. Quest. How far are men bound according to their abilitie and meanes to reach out their helping hands for the reliefe of such as ought to bee relieued, bing any way distressed in their bodies, and knowne to them by sight or by hearing, to stand in need of reliefe in respect of their bodies? Answ. Sometimes to the entertainment of them to bed or board, or both,Iob. 31.32. Iudg. 19.20.21. Rom. 12.13. Heb. 13.2. 1 Pet. 4.9. especially they being strangers and har∣bourlesse, and for the Lords cause, and for a good conscience persecuted. This dutie of entertaing of strangers and harbourlesse, was peculiar to the primue Church, when Christians were banished and thrust out  house and home, and wandered vp and downe in the time of the tenne bloody persecutions, and therefore not now to be practised. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; In those times there was greater need of the practice of this dutie, then now in the setled state of the Church, but yet it reacheth to all times, and that appears by the sentence that Christ shall giue on the Sheepe and Goats, Mah. 25. it is sayd, verse 32, 33, 34, 35, 36, &c. As Gods prouidence shall offer strangers to vs harbourlesse and persecuted: so wee are to giue them entertainement ac∣cording to our abilitie. Quest. To whom are men chiefly bound according to their abilitie and meanes to reach out their hlping hands for their reliefe, being any way distressed in their bodies, and knowne to them to stand in need of reliefe, in respect of their bodies? Answ. To such as they are bound to by some neere and speciall bond of place, calling, or condition,Iob 19.13. to 22. Leuit. 25.35. Rom. 12.13. Galat. 6.10. or of nature or grace, as to Father, Mother, Husband, Wife, Children, Master, Seruant, or to the Saints and children of God. Quest. What if a man be able to releeue but one being in
want, and distresse of body, and his owne father or mother and his owne childe are at the same time in like want and distresse of body, and knowne to him so to bee: which of them is he then to releeue? Mat. 15.4.5.6. Mar. 7.10.11.12.Answ. Rather his father or his mother then his childe, because hee owes more debt and dutie to his parents, from whom hee had his substance and being, then to his children, who haue their substance and being from him: therefore Christ preferres the releeuing of parents before Free-will offerings. Quest. VVhat if a man, bee able to releeue but one being in want and distresse of body; and his owne father or mother be∣ing not religious, and another that is not of his kindred being re∣ligious and fearing God, are at the same time in like want and distresse of body, and knowne to them so to be: which of them is he then to relieue? Answ. Rather his father or mother then the other partie, because hee is thereunto bound, both by the bond of Nature in speciall manner, and also by religion, and by the comman∣dement of God. Math. 12.49, 50. Christ esteemes his Disciples, and doth esteeme those that doth the will of God his Father, and so are religious and truely feare God, as his brethren, and as his mother, and so are we to esteeme of them: therefore we are to releeue such as are religious, though not of our kindred, ra∣ther then our father or mother that are not religious, being at the same time in like want and distresse of body, and knowne to vs so to be. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; wee are indeed to esteeme such as are reli∣gious, being not of our kindred, as deare to vs as our pa∣rents, as they stand in relation onely to vs; but when they come in comparison with our parents, and they and our parents though not religious, are set before vs at the same time in like want and distresse of body, wee are not then to releeue them, and to neglect our parents: for so doing wee sinne not onely against Religion, but against the Law of na∣ture also.
Quest. What if a man bee able to releeue but one in want and distresse of body; and a stranger or an enemy is in extreme want and distresse of body; and like to perish, and a friend or a kinsman is in great want and distresse, but not in such extremitie, and the want and distresse of both is knowne to him: which of them is he then to releeue? Answ. Rather the stranger or his enemy,Mat. 5.44. Luk. 6.35. Rom. 12.20. then his friend or kinsman: for the state and condition of men or women in want and distresse of body is principally to be respected, without any difference of persons. Quest. Is the body of another onely to be respected while it is aliue, and is nothing to be done vnto it when it is dead? Answ. Yes, there is a dutie belongs to the dead body of another. Qu. What is the dutie that belongs to the dead body of another? Answ. The buriall of it in such honest and seemely man∣ner,Gen. 23.19. Gen. 25.9 Gen. 50.13. Iere. 22.19. as is agreeable to the nature and credit as well of those which remaine aliue, as of the partie deceased, with mode∣rate mourning. Mat. 24.60. Acts 8.2. 1 Thes. 4.13. Now to the things that tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the soule of man, and to the welfare and safetie of mans soule. Quest. What are the things that tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the soule of man, and to the welfare and safetie of the soule? Answ. They are either such things as tend to the main∣tenance and preseruation of the life of a mans owne soule, and the welfare and safetie of his owne soule: or such things as tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the soule of another or others, and to the welfare and safetie of the soule of another or others. Quest. What are the things that tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of a mans owne soule, and to the welfare and safetie of his owne soule? Answ. Two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; a carefull auoyding of all such things as tend to the destroying of his own soule, as all sorts of sinnes,
especially knowne sinnes,Pro. 11.19. Rom. 2.5. 1 Pet. 3.20.11. and liuing and continuing in any knowne sinne willingly and obstinately, and with delight. Quest. What is the second thing that tends to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of a mans owne soule, and to the welfare and safetie of his owne soule? Deut. 30.19.20 Rom. 10.14.17 1 Pet. 2.2. Pro. 16.17.Answ. This; a carefull vse of the meanes that God hath ordained both for the beginning, and for the continuance of grace and of spirituall life in the soule, both in publike, and in priuate; as of the word of God preached or read, Sacra∣ments, Prayer, and the like. Quest. How do men carefully vse the meanes God hath ordai∣ned for the beginning, and for the continuance of grace, and of spi∣rituall life in the soule? Pro. 2.1.2.3.4. Pro. 4.20.21. Pro: 7.1.2.3.4. Pro. 8.33. Isai. 55.3.Answ. By diligent attending on them, and by vsing them conscionably, and with care to be bettered and to profit by them: this we find required in many places of Scripture. Co∣loss. 3.16. 1 Thes. 2.13. Quest. How doe men carefully walke in the way of life, and of saluation?Ephes. 2.10. Philip: 2.12. 2 Pet. 4.5.6. to 12. Psal. 92.14. 2 Pet: 3.18. Answ. By diligence to finish their owne saluation, by ad∣ding daily one measure of grace to another, and by making their owne calling and election sure by the fruits of faith. Quest. What are the things that tend to the maintenance and preseruation of the life of the soule of another or others, and to the welfare and safety of the soule of another or others? Answ. Such things as serue for the procuring or helping forward of the spirituall life and saluation of another or o∣thers: men are as they are able, and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offered, to pro∣cure or to helpe forward the spirituall life and saluation of another or others.1 Cor. 10.33. Quest. How are men, as they are able and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offered, to procure and to helpe forward the spirituall life and saluation of another or o∣thers? Pro. 11.30. Dan. 12.3. Rom. 15.2. Iam. 5 19.20.Answ. By doing such things as tend to the winning of their soules, and to their edification in grace & goodnes. Quest. What are the things that men are to doe tending to the
winning of the soules of others, and to their edification in grace and goodnesse? Answ. Sixe things especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. This; they are as they are able,Gen. 18.19. Deut. 6.7. Pro. 1.10. P o 31.1. Ioh. 1.35. to 45 Act. 20.26.27. Coloss. 3.16. and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offered, to teach and to instruct others to knowe God, and the good wayes of God; and to counsell, and to aduise them in suh things as concerne their sanctification and saluation, e∣specially such as bee vnder their charge; they being such as haue the gouernment of others, and are ouer others in publike or in priuate, as Ministers and Gouernours in the family. Quest. May not inferiours sometimes teach and instruct, ad∣uise and counsell their Superiours? Answ. Yes, they may,1 Sam. 25.23. to 32. Iob. 31.13. Act. 18.26. and they ought sometimes to teach and instruct their Superiours, finding them fit and willing to bee taught, instructed, aduised, and counselled by them, and dealing with them with reuerence, and with humilitie. Math. 28.19. Ministers are commanded to teach and bap∣tize, and so it belongs to the Ministers of the Word onely to teach others; and therefore not to Gouernours in the family. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; it belongs to the Ministers of the Word onely to teach as Ministers; but yet gouernors in the family may teach as gouernors in another kind of teaching. Quest. VVherein stands the difference betweene the teaching of the Ministers of the Word, and the teaching of Gouernours in the family? Answ. In two things. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; Ministers of the Word teach in the name of God, and by authority from Christ, as in his roome and stead,Tit 2.15. 2 Cor. 5.19.20 and as his Ambassadors: and hence they are called Men of God, seruants of God; but Gouernors in the family teach only by the authoritie of an husband, a father or master. Quest. What is the second difference betweene the teaching of the Ministers of the word, and of gouernors in a family?
Answ. This; the teaching of Ministers of the Word de∣pends onely on the teaching of Gods Spirit by his Word.Ezech. 3.17. Deut. 18.18. 2 Cor. 3.8. But the teaching of Gouernors in a family depends on pub∣like teaching, and must be ordered by it; and they must teach nothing but that they haue learned and receiued from the publike Ministery, and is agreeable to it. Quest. What is the second thing that men are to doe tending to the winning of the soules of others, and to their edification and building vp in grace and goodnesse? Answ. This; they are as they are able, and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offered, to prouoke and to excite and stirre vp others to holinesse and to well doing, and to hearten, and to encourage them in well doing, especially such as bee vnder their charge, they being such as haue the gouernment of others.Pro: 27.17. Heb. 10.34. Prou. 27.17. A man is to whet his friend to knowledge, ioy, loue, diligence, and Zeale. Quest. How are men, as they are able, and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offered, to prouoke, and to excite, and to stirre vp others to weldoing, and to hearten and to encourage them in well doing? 2 Chron. 19.9. 2 Chron. 20.20 2 Chron. 32.7. 1 Thess. 5.11. 1 Tim. 5.1.2. Hebr. 3.13. Rom. 1.3. 1 Cor. 11.2.Answ. By perswading and by exhorting them to good things, and by praising, commending, and countenancing them when they doe well. Quest. What is the third thing that men are to doe tending to the winning of the soules of others, and their edification and buil∣ding vp in grace and goodnesse? Answ. This; they are, as they are able, and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offe∣red, to admonish and to reproue others, when they see or know them to offend and to doe euill, and to sinne, so as they de it fitly and seasonably. Quest. How doe men reproue others fitly? Answ. When their reproofe is fited to the quality of the person whom they reproue,Leuit. 19.17. Luke 17 3. Coloss. 3.16. 1 Thess. 5.14. 2 Tim. 2.4. Tit. 2.15. and to the nature and quality of the off nce for which the person i reproued. Quest. How is the reproofe fitted to the quality of the per∣son reproued?
Answ. Thus; when men reproue their equalls louingly and friendly,Gal. 6.1. 1 Tim. 5.1. 2 Sam. 12.1. Tit. 3.13. Nehem. 5.7. Iob 2.20. Prou. 29.17.19 their Superiours (hauing a calling so to doe) by reuerent and humble exhortation; their Inferiours sharpely, the fact being notorious, scandalous, or dan∣gerous: and such of their Inferiours as ouer whom they haue speciall authoritie, as their Children, Seruants, Subiects, or the like, sometimes by due chastisement and correction. Quest. How is reproofe fitted to the nature and quality of the offence, for which the person is reproued? Answ. Thus; when men reprooue others for sinnes and offences committed of ignorance or frailtie,Iude epist. ver. 22.23. 2 Cor. 13.2. with gentle∣nesse; and for sins and offences committed of malice, pride, and presumption, with sharpnesse and seueritie. Quest. How doe men reprooue others seasonably? Answ. When they doe it in such a time as the reproofe may doe them most good: as when they discerne them to be willing to hare reproofe, they are no scorners,Psal. 141.5. Prou. 9.8. 1 Sam. 25.36.37 and that they are capable of reproofe, they are not drunke, nor in heat of passion. Quest. VVhat if men being but priuate persons, doe know another or others to practice some thing that tends to the hurt of the Church or Common-wealth; as to plot Treason, or to inter-meddle in treasonable practices, or the like, are they then priuate∣ly to admonish and to reproue them? Answ. In such a case they are not, but they are then to discouer them to the publike Magistrate,Deut. 13.6.7.8 9 Hest. 2.21.22. that by him they may bee dealt withall according to the nature and qualitie of the offence. Question VVhat if men beeing but priuate persons, doe knowe another or others, to intend to kill and to murder another, and to lye in wayte purposely to take away his life, are they then priuately to admonish and to reprooue them? Answ. No; in this case also they are bound to discouer them to the publike Magistrate:Act. 23.16.17. for the life of a man or wo∣man is to be preferred before the credit of such as seeke vn∣iustly to take it away.
Quest. What is the fourth thing that men are to doe tending to the winning of the soules of others, and to their edification and building vp in grace and goodnesse? Answ. This; they are as they are able, and according to their place and calling,Gen. 50.21. Sam. 23.16. Sam. 10.2. ob 6 14.15. sai. 40.1.2. Mat. 14.27. 1 Thess. 4.18. 1 Thess. 5.14 and as the present occasion is offered, to comfort others, when they see or know them to stand in need of comfort, in regard of their troubles and distresses, e∣specially in regard of the troubles and distresses and afflicti∣ons of their minds and consciences for sinne, so as they doe it wisely and seasonably. Quest. How doe men wisely and seasonably comfort others that are troubled and afflicted in their minds & consciences for sinne? Answ. When they duly consider the person afflicted, as whether it be a man or woman, young or old, hauing know∣ledge or wanting knowledge, whether by nature fearefull and melancholike or no, whether a vsuall sinner or no, and the like, and accordingly to apply comfort: and when they doe it in such a time as comfort may doe the partie affcted most good; as when they discerne the partie afflicted to bee fit for comfort,Iob 16.2. Iob 19.21. Isai. 50.4. as being humbled rather for sinne then for outward shame, or the like, and not grieued onely with a generall notion and sight of sinne, but extreamely throwne downe with the burden of particular sinnes. Quest. VVhat is the fift thing that men are to doe tending to the winning of the soules of others, and to their edification and building vp in grace and goodnesse? Answ. This; they are as they are able, and according to their place and calling,Ier. 42.2.3. Gen. 43.29. Gen 48.15. 1 Chro. 22.12. Iam. 5.15. and as present occasion is offered, to pray for others standing in need of their prayers, for the good of their soules, and especially such as they are bound to, by some neere and speciall bond, as of nature or of grace, or of place or calling, and condition, and the like. Quest. What is the sixt thing that men are to doe tending to the winning of the soules of others, and to their edification and building vp in grace and goodnesse? Answ. This; they are as they are able, and according to their place and calling, and as present occasion is offered to giue good example to others,Math. 5.1. 2 Cor. 9.2. liuing in their sight without
giuing iust offence, and walking before them in the practice of good things, especially to such as they are bound to,1 Pet 2.12. 1 Pet. 3.1. by some neare and speciall bond of nature, place, calling or condition. Now to the seauenth Commandement Exod 20.14. Thou shalt not commit Adultery. Quest. Why is the Commandement that forbids Adultery, netxt to that that forbids Killing or Murder? Answ. For this reason, because next after iniurie done to the person of man or woman,Gen. 2.24. Mat. 19.5. 1 Cor. 6.16. there is none greater then that which is offered or done to the ioynt person: as the wife is to the Husband, and the Husband to the Wife, they two being but one flesh. Quest. What are the words of the seauenth Commandement? Answ. Those we finde, Exod. 20.14. Thou shalt not com∣mit Adulterie. Quest. What is the meaning of the words of this Comman∣dement? Answ. This; thou shalt not thinke, will, speake,Mat. 5.18. 2 Cor. 7.1. 1 Thess. 4.3.4. or doe any thing whereby thine owne chastitie, or the chastitie of a∣nother or others may be hurt or hindered. Quest. What is the-ground of this prohibition: thou shalt not thinke, will, speake, or doe any thing whereby thine owne chasti∣tie, or the chastitie of another or others may be hurt or hindered? Answ. Both the preseruation of a speciall part of Gods I∣mage in man,Gen: 20.9. Gen: 26.10. chastity being a speciall part of Gods Image in man; and therefore Adultery is knowne to be a sinne by the light of nature: and also the propagation of an holy seede to be made by man on earth, God hauing appointed one man to one woman to that end. Mat. 2.15.Mat: 2.15. Quest. Why is Adultery heere named, rather then any other sin of the same kinde? Answ. For two reasons especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ, This; because it breakes the couenant of marri∣age,Pro: 2.17. whereby married persons bind themselues not only one with another but to God himselfe (who hath appointed the Ordinance of Marriage) th they will faithfully and truely
keepe their faith plighted one to the other. Quest. What is the second reason why Adulterie is heere na∣med, rather then any other sin of the same kinde? Answ. This: because it brings pollution into the Ordi∣nance which God hath sanctified for the propagation of an holy seede, and makes confusion in Stocks and Families through bastardy: and many times brings the child of the A∣dulterer into another mans possession, to his great wrong and indignity. Quest. What is the summe of this Commandement? Answ. That chastitie bee not any way hurt or hindered, either in our selues or in others, but that both in our selues & in others,Tit. 2.5. it be euery way and by all good meanes preserued, Ioseph was carefull of his. Gen. 39, 9.Gen. 39.9. Now this Commandement being Negatiue: I will first shew what this Commandement forbids. Quest. What doth this Commandement forbid? Answ. In generall, all manner of vncleanes, and fleshly defilement: and all things that doe hurt or hinder chastity in man or woman. Quest. What are the things that doe hurt or hinder chastity in man or woman? Answ. They are either things inward in the heart, or out∣ward things. Quest. What are the inward things in the heart, that do hurt or hinder chastity in man or woman? Answ. They are filthy imaginations, and vnchast thoughts, and inward lusts and motions of the heart to vncleannesse,Mate. 5.28. Coloss. 3.5. whereunto the heart doth giue consent: or purposes and de∣sires of the heart to any act of vncleannes, and fleshly de∣filement. Quest. When are inward lusts and motions of the heart to vncleannesse, whereunto the heart giues consent, most vile and odious? Answ. When they are so violent and strong, as that they continually boyle and burne within, and giue a man or woman no rest,1 Cor. 7.9. but are euer stirring and prouoking them to
the committing of some filthy act of vncleannesse: 1 Cor. 7 9 It is better to marry then to burne, (that is) to haue within a continuall feruencie of lusts, in the heart.Hosea 7.4. Coloss. 3.5.Coloss. 3.5. inor∣dinate affection. Quest. VVhat are the outward things that doe hurt or hin∣der chastity in man or woman? Answ. They are either things going before the act of vn∣cleannesse and fleshly pollution: or the act of vncleannesse and fleshly pollution it selfe. Quest. What are the things that goe before the act of vnclean∣nesse and fleshly pollution? Answ. Either things farther of, as preparatiues and pro∣uocations to it: or things nearer to it. Quest. What are the preparatiues and prouocations to the act of vncleannesse? Answ. They are either such things as stirre vp filthy lust, and make the body fit for vncleannes: or such things as helpe forward that fitnesse. Quest. What are the things that stirre vp filthy lust, and make the body fit for vncleannes? Answ. Foure especiall. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. Gluttony, or excesse in eating and pampering of the belly with meates:Ier. 5.8. Ezech. 16.49. Rom. 13.13. Hosea 7.6. as when men or women either eate ordinary meates immoderately, till they doe thereby glut themselues, or they vse delicates and curious dainty meates deliciously and vnseasonably, especially such as haue grea∣test force to encrease and to stirre vp filthy lust, purposely to encrease and to stirre it vp in themselues. Quest. What is the second thing that stirrs vp filthy lust, and makes the body fit for vncleannesse? Answ. This; Drunkennesse or excesse in drinking,Gen. 19.32.33.34.35. Prou. 23.30.31.33. as when men or women doe take into their bodies strong drinke, Ale, Beare, Wine, or compound water exces∣siuely till they doe thereby surchage nature, and disorder the powers of reason, and inrage their naturall affections, and pecially when thy doe vse wines and strong drinkes, wantonly and vnseasonably, and of purpose to stirre vp
filthy lust:sai. 5.11. om. 13.13. phes. 5.18. after drunkennesse followes chambering and wantonnesse, omnis profusio et turpitudo. Quest. What is the third thing that stirrs vp filthy lust, and makes the body fit for vncleanesse? Answ. This; lustfull dreames comming from surfeiting and drunkennes. Hence come nocturnall pollutions spoken of, Deut. 23.10. Quest. What is the fourth thing that stirrs vp filthy lust, and makes the body fit for vncleanesse? Answ. This; Idlenesse, as when men or women spend their strength and time God giues them,2 Sam: 11.1.2. Ezech: 16.49. 1 Tim. 5.13. wherein they ought to be imployed in some honest labours of minde or body, in ex∣cessiue sleeping, and in sluggishnesse, in ease and in doing nothing; but following their sensuall pleasures. Quest. What are the things that helpe forward the fitnesse of the body for vncleannesse? Answ. Seauen especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; any light, vaine, immodest, either setting out of the body, or carriage of the body; as by riotus, lasci∣uious,Ezech. 16.49. Pro. 7:10. 1 Tim: 2.9. 1 Pet. 3.3. 1 Cor. 11.14. 2 King. 9.30. Iere. 4.30. Isai. 3.16. to 24 garish, disguised, and new fangled attire; by long shag hayre, by platting, cutling, frizling, powdering, or colou∣ring of the haire; by painting the face, by laying out the naked breasts, by stretching out the necke, by mincing or tinkling with the feete. Quest. May not men or women seeing a fashion of attire vsed in a strange Countrey and not in vse in their owne Countrey, take it vp and vse it in their owne Countrey? Answ. No, they may not: the Lord hath threatned to vi∣site such as weare strange apparrell. Zephan. 1.8.Zephan. 1.8. Quest. May not a man or a woman hauing some deformity in his or her body, labour to couer it? Answ. Yes, they may; so as they set not a new forme or face, or a new habit on the body: for dissembling is vnlaw∣full aswell in deede as in word. Isaie prophesied naked, therefore it may seeme lawfull to lay out the bare breasts. Quest. How is this to be answered?
Answ. Thus; that which the Prophet did, was done by the especiall commandement of God, and to a speciall end; and therefore is not to be imitated. Quest. VVhat is the second thing that helpes forward the fitnesse of the body for vncleannesse? Answ. This; the keeping company with lasciuious, wan∣ton, and fleshly persons: and frequenting of lewd houses,Gen. 39.10. Psal. 50.18. Pro. 5.8. Pro. 7.7.8.9.10. &c. Ephes: 5, 5, 7 houses of filthinesse: when men or women ordinarily, with∣out any warrant or calling, keepe company with filthy per∣sons, and frequent lewd houses, especially at vnseasonable times. Quest. VVhat is the third that helpes forward the fit∣nesse of the body for vncleannesse? Ans. This; immodest, vnchast, ribald and filthy spea∣king, when men or women vtter rotten and filthy speeches,Ephes. 4.29. Ephes. 5.3.4. Coloss. 3.8. tell filthy tales, or sing songs, and sonnets, and ballads of loue and lightnesse, and of abhominable filthinesse, rotten speeches. Quest: What is the fourth thing that helpes forward the fit∣nesse of the body for vncleannesse? Answ: This; reading of vnchast and filthy bookes; bookes of loue matters and daliance, and filthinesse: 1 Corin 15.33.1 Cor. 15.33.  some render the words euill speakings, or euill communication, some euill conuersings: I take it, we may vnder∣stand the word thus, conuersing with others in their euill spea∣kings, sayings or writings: and so reading of vile and filthy bookes, fitter to be burnt as these were. Act. 19.19. Quest. What is the fift thing that helpes forward the fitnesse of the body for vncleannesse? Answ. This; idle and curious looking of men on women, or of women on men; when men or women curiously looke on the beauty, feature, and proportion of the body one of another:2 Sam: 11.2. Iob. 31.1. 2 Pet: 2.14. thus did the sonnes of God behold the daughters of men, Gen. 6.2.Gen: 6.2. Thus Potiphars wife beheld Ioseph. Gen. 39.7.Gen: 39.7. Gen. 34.1.2.Gen. 34.1.2. Dinah went out to see the Daughters of the Land, and when Shechem saw her, he tooke her and lay with her, and defiled her? Quest. May not a man looke on the beauty of a woman, or
a woman looke on the beauty of a man, and sin not? King. 10.7.8Answ. Yes, they may; and they ought thereby to take occasion to glorifie God, as the Queene of Sheba by behold∣ing Salomons person, and hearing his wisedome, did take oc∣casion to glorifie God. Quest. What is the sixt thing that helpes forward the fitnesse of the body for vncleannesse? Ans. This; the looking on lasciuious, filthy and vnseem∣ly pictures,Nomb. 25:1.2.3. Ezech: 23.14. Ephes. 5.3.4. and the beholding of filthinesse, loue matters, and light behauiour of men and women, represented and set out, not only by speech, but by gesture and by conuaiances and deuices in Stage Playes and Comedies. The Israelites were brought to fornication by the sight of the filthy Idoll Baall Peor. Quest. What is the seauenth thing that helpes forward the fitnesse of the body for vncleannesse? Answ. This; immodest and wanton dancing, mixt dan∣cing of men and women together,Exod. 32.6. Iob. 21.11.12. Mar. 6.21.22. in number and measure artificially: especially after solemne feasts, and at merry meetings, with many wanton and lasciuious gestures ac∣companying the same. Exod. 22.6. The people sate downe to eate and drinke  and they rose vp to play. (that is) as the best interpreters say, to dance wantonly af∣ter they had eaten and drunken, Iob. 21.11.12. Mar. 6.21.22. after the banquet Herod made the daughter of Herodias come skipping and dancing in, to please Herod, wherewith his a∣morous and lustfull eye was entangled, and Iohn Baptists head begged. Quest. What are the things going before the act of vncleanness and fleshly pollution, nearer to it then preparatiues or prouocations vnto it? Answ. They are three things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; vsing and wearing of apparrell not fit for the sexe,Deut. 22:5. Iob 24.15. Gen. 38.15. as when men put on and goe in womens apparell; or women put on and goe in mens apparell, that they may not bee knowne, but may more easily come to commit fil∣thinesse.
Quest. What is the second thing going before the act of vnclean∣nesse, and nearer to it then preparatiues or prouocations? Answ. This; wanton kissing, and imbracing, and vn∣chast touching and dalliance:Gen. 39.12. Pro. 7.13. Deut. 25.11.12 when men or women do wan∣tonly kisse or embrace one another, or doe vnchastly touch or dallie one with another. Quest. VVhat is the third thing going before the act of vn∣cleannesse and fleshly pollution, and nearer to it then preparatiues or prouocations? Answ. This; mouing, intising, and perswading to the very act of vncleannesse and fleshly pollution,Gen. 39.7.10 12 Pro. 7.13 to 21 as Iosephs Mistress did, she was not ashamed to moue him with her own mouth to lye with her. Quest. What are the acts of vncleannesse and fleshly pollution that hurt or hinder chastity in men or women? Answ. They are either with ones selfe or with others. Quest. How is chastity hurt or hindered in man or woman with themselues? Answ. By effeminate wantonnesse,Gen. 38▪9. 1 Cor. 6.9. and by doing as Onan did: when men or women abuse their owne bodyes, and by any way or meanes doe prouoke and procure themselues to doe as Onan did. Gen. 38.9. The Apostle calls them that so doe, effeminate persons or wantons. 1 Cor. 6.9. Quest. How is chastity hurt or hindered in man or woman with others? Answ. Either with one other, or with many others. Quest. How is chastity hurt or hindered in man or woman with one other alone? Answ. Thus; either by married persons, man and wife be∣tweene themselues, or by others that are not marryed one to another. Quest. How is chastity hurt or hindered by married persons, man and wife betweene themselues? Answ. Either in respect of their enterance into marriage, or in regard of their after proceeding and vse of it. Q. How is chastity hurt or hindred by married persons, man & wife betweene thēselues, in respect of their enterance into marryage? Answ. Thus; when they company together and haue secret
society one with another as man & wife, & yet are either such as entred into that state and condition,Exod. 22.16.17. Deut: 7.3. Iere. 29.6. 1 Cor: 7.38. Leuit. 18.6. to 18. Leuit. 20.19 20.21. Mar: 6.18. 1 Cor. 5.10. without the due con∣sent of their parents, neither hauing it at the time of their en∣trance, nor hauing gotten it afterwards; or they are such as ought not to haue married together, being within the de∣grees of Consanguinity or Affinity, forbidden in the Word of God. Quest. May cosen germans, brothers children, or sisters chil∣dren marry together or no? Answ. The marriage of cosen germans is not expresly forbidden in the Word of God, yet in sundry respects being inconuenient and inexpedient, it ought not to be done accor∣ding to the saying of the Apostle, 1 Cor. 10.23. All things are lawfull for me, but all things are not expedient. Quest. May a man after his wife is dead, marry her sister or no? Answ. No, hee may not; for as a woman may not mar∣rie with two brothers, one after another, Leuit. 18.16. Leuit. 20.21. so a man may not marry with two sisters, there the same proportion holds both wayes. Leuit. 18.18. The Lord doth not there forbid a man to marry two sisters, one after another; but to marry them both together, and therefore after a wife is dead, a man may mar∣rie her sister. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; that place is thus to be read, thou shalt not take a woman to her sister; that is one woman to another, and it is not to be vnderstood of marrying two sisters together; but of hauing of two wies or women together, and so it proues not that after the wife is dead, a man may marry her sister. Deut. 25.5. The Lord commanded that a man dying with∣out Issue, his brother should take his wife and raise vp seede to him: and therefore it seemes lawfull for a woman to marry two brothers, and so for a man to marry two sisters, Quest. How is this to be answered Answ. Thus; those words are a speciall exception of that law, Leuit. 18.16. & are peculiarly directed to the Israelites,
and did giue them only that libertie for a time, for the conti∣nuance and preseruation of their Tribes and Families di∣stinct one from another till the comming of the Messiah: and that priuiledge must not be extended to any other sort of men whatsoeuer. The prohibitions Leuit. 18. are Mosaicall and ceremoniall, and therefore do not bind vs now vnder the New Testament. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; Those prohibitions are grounded on the law of Nature, for God did cast the Canaanites out of the Land, who had only the law of Nature to guide them, and were not bound to the ceremoniall Law of Moses, because they were therein defiled,Ezech. 22.10. Mar. 6.18. 1 Cor. 5.1. Leuit. 18.24.25. therefore they are morall; and so they are accounted both by the Prophets, and also in the New Testament. Quest. How is chastity hurt or hindered by married persons, man and wife betweene themselues, in regard of their after procee∣ding and vse of marriage? Answ. Two wayes. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; when they vse the marriage bed intempe∣rately and immoderately, not for procreation, or for yeeld∣ing due debt one to another, or for the auoyding of for∣nication; but meerely for the satisfying of their vnbridled pleasures: for as a man may be a drunkard by taking into his body his owne strong drinke excessively, and a glutton by excessiue deuouring of his owne meate: so may one bee fil∣thy & vncleane by the immoderate vse of the Marriage bed. 1 Thes. 4.4.5. not to doe any thing vnbeseeming honestie and temperance of Marriage. Heb. 13.4. Marriage (being vsed as it ought) is honourable amongst all. Quest. What is the second way by which chastitie is hurt or hindered by married persons, man and wife betweene themselues in regard of the vsed of their marriage? Answ. This; when they company together and vse the marriage bed vnseasonably. Quest. How doe married persons companie together and vse their marriage bed vnseasonably?
Answ. Two wayes Quest. What is the first of those? Gen. 18.11. Leuit. 18.19. Leuit. 20.18. Ezech. 18.6. Ezech. 22.10.Answ. This; if they company together and know each other whilst it is with the woman after the manner of women: as Gene. 18.11. when God and nature reqire that they should forbeare the marriage bed, and keepe themselues a∣sundr. Quest. What is the second way by which married persons com∣pany together and vse their marriage bed vnseasonably? Answ. This; if they company togther and know each o∣ther in the time of publike humiliation; in the time of a so∣lemne fast vsed in regard of some grieuous calamity,2 Sam. 11.11. Ioel. 2.16. Zach. 12.12. 1 Cor. 7.5. either imminent and like to fall on the Church or common Wealth, or already on it: when they ought to giue themselues by mutuall consent, to fasting and prayer. Quest. How is chastity hurt or hindered in man or wo∣man one with another alone by such as are not married one to another? Answ. Two wayes. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; when such as are not married one to ano∣ther, doe commit some act of vncleannesse and fleshly defile∣ment one with another, which is vnnatural & against nature. Quest. How do such as are not married one to another commit some act of vncleannesse and fleshly defilement one with another, which is vnnaturall and against nature? Answ. Thre wayes, Quest. Which is the first of those? Leuit. 18.22. Leuit. 2.13. Rom. 1.26.27. 1 Cor. 6.9. 1 Tim. 1.10.Answ. This; by Sodomitrie, or by committing the sinne of Sodome, which is vncleannesse and defilement of the body committd betweene them that are of one and the sme sexe; as by man with man, or by woman with woman. Quest. Why is this sinne called Sodomitrie, or the sinne of Sodome? Answ. Because the Sodomites are the first wee read off to haue committed this sinne,Ge. 19.4.5.6.7 and they were outragious in the committing of it. Quest. How doth this sin appeare to be a great & grieuous sin?
Answ. Both bcause the light of nature condemnes it, and because it is commonly a punishment of other foule sins; and because also it is a sinne, which they commit whom God hath giuen vp to a reprobate sense Rom 1.26.27.Rom. 1.26.27. Quest. What is the second way by which such as are not mar∣ried one with another, commit the act of vncleannes & fleshly de∣filement one with another, which is vnnaturall & against nature? Answ. This; by beastiality which is vncleannesse and de∣filement of the body, committed by man or woman with a bruite beast, forbidden Leuit. 18.23.Leuit. 18.23. and condemned to death, Leuit. 20.15.16.Leuit. 20.15.16 Q. What is the third way by which such as are not married one with another, commit some act of vncleanness & fleshly defilement one with another, which is vnnaturall and against nature? Answ. This; by vncleannesse and fleshly defilement of the body, committed by man or woman with the Deuill; as Witches doe, by their owne confession: for the Deuil may appeare in a bodily shape, and may sometimes (the Lord suf∣fering him) vse the body of a man or woman as hee vsed the body of the Serpent: Gen. 3.1.Gen. 3.1. and so may haue company with those, who either haue familiarity with him, or giue themselues much to filthinesse. Q. What is the second way by which chastity is hurt or hindred, with one other alone, by such as are not married one to another? Answ. This; when such as are not married one to another, doe commit some act of vncleannesse and fleshly defilement one with another which is naturall, and according to the course of nature corrupted. Quest. How doe such as are not married one to another, com∣mit some act of vncleannesse and fleshly defilement one with another which is naturall, and according to the course of nature corrupted? Answ. Two wayes.Gen. 19.33. to 37. Gen 35.2. Gen 49.4. Gen. 8.18. 2 Sam. 13.14. Ezech. 22.11 Mar. 6.18. 1 Cor. 5.1. Quest. Which is the first of those? Answ. This; by committing the sinne of Incest, which is vncleannesse and defilement of the body, committed be∣tweene man and woman that are neere in bloud & of kindred one to another, either by consanguinity or affinitie.
Quest. What is the second way by which such as are not mar∣ried one to another, doe commit some act of vncleannesse and flesh∣ly defilement one with another which is naturall, and according to the course of nature corrupted? Answ. This; by vncleannesse and defilement of the body, committed betweene man and woman, that are not neere in blood, nor of kindred one to another, either by consanguini∣tie or affinitie. Qust. How is that done? Answ. Two waies. Quest. What is the first of those? Gen. 34.2. 1. Cor. 6.9.18. 1 Cor. 10.8. Coloss. 3.5. Heb. 13.4.Answ. This; by fornication, which is vncleannesse and fleshly defilement of the body committed betweene man and woman being both single and vnmarried persons. Here some things saide in dfence of fornication are to be answered. Gen. 19 8. Lot offered his daughters to the men of Sodome when they called for the strangers that were come into his house to abuse them, which (say some) hee would not haue done if fornication had beene a sinne: therefore it seemes that fornication is no sinne. Quest. How is this to be answered? Ans. Thus; that fact of Lot cannot be iustified nor ex∣cused, it was euill and a sinne; though his purpose was by a lesser euill to preuent a greater; for no man may do the least euill or sinne for the procuring of the greatest good that can be. Rom. 3.8. And so that fact of his proues not fornication to be no sinne. 2 Pet. 2.7. The Apostle cals Lot a iust man, therefore hee was blamelesse in that fact of his, in offering his daughters to the rage of the Sodomites. Quest: How is this to be answered? Answ: Thus; though Lot be called a iust man, yet it fol∣lowes not that euery particular act of his was iust, for then his incest with his two daughters might finde defence. Hosea. 1.2. The Lord commanded Hosea to take a wife of fornication; therefore fornication is not simply euill, and in it selfe a sinne. Quest. How is this to be answered?
Answ. Thus; that which the Prophet did (if he did take a wife of fornication) he did it not of his owne head, but by Gods speciall appointment who is Lord of his owne law, and may dispense with it at his owne pleasure, as hee com∣manded Abraham to kill his sonne Izaack. Gen. 22.2. which if Abraham had done he had not sinned, though the sixt Commandement forbid killing and murder: because he had Gods speciall commandement for it; so that fact of Hosea proues not that fornication is not simply euill, and in it selfe no sinne. Acts. 15.29. The Apostles reckon vp fornication amongst things indifferent, therefore it is a thing indifferent. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; it followes not, that fornication is a thing indifferent, because in that place it is ioyned with things in∣diffrent; for it was not the purpose of the Apostles to shew what things were indifferent, or what vnlawfull, but what thigs were most offnsiue, and what things did chiefely trouble the Churches and offend the weake Iewes, and and those were eating of blood, and things strangled, and the fornication of the Gentiles. Quest. What is the second way by which vncleannesse and de∣filement of the body is committed betweene man and woman that are not neere in blood nor of kindred one to another, either by con∣sanguinitie or affinitie?Gen. 26.10. Leuit. 18.20. Leuit. 20.10. 2 Sam. 11.4. Ier. 5.7.8. 1 Cor. 6.9. Heb. 13.4. Deut. 22.2.23.24. Answ. By Adultery which is vncleannesse and defile∣ment of the body, committed betweene man and woman, be∣ing either both of them married persons, or one of them a married person, or at the least contracted. Quest. Is Adultery a more grieuous sinne in man or in wo∣man, or is it equally as great and as grieuous a sinne in the one as in the other? Answ. In some respect it is a more grieuous sinne in the man, and in some respect it is a more grieuous sinne in the woman, and in some respect it is equally as great and grie∣uous a sinne in the one as in the other. Quest: In what respect is Adultery a more grieuous sinne in the man then in the woman?
1 Pet. 3.7. Ephes. 5.23. 2 Sam. 12.1.14Answ. In respect of the quality and condition of the per∣son, because the woman is the weaker vessell, and the man is the head of the woman, and is or ought to bee more strong; and because also his example, especially hee being a publike person doth more hurt. 2 Sam. 12. Nathan is sent to Dauid, not to Bathsheba, because his example did more hurt. Quest. In what respect is Adultery a more grieuous sinne in the woman then in the man? Answ. In respect of the inconueniences that follow on it, as ignominie and shame of houses, and families confusion of inheritances & thrusting of false Heires in the place & roome of true and lawfull Heires. Quest. In what respect is adultery a sinne equally as great and grieuous in both sexes in the man as in the woman, and in the woman as in the man? Leuit. 20.10. Deut. 22.22.23Answ. In respect of the speciall and particular law of marriage, where by the husband and wife are bound one to another equally, and that most neerely and most strictly: the sinne is equall in both Sexes, therefore the Apostle saith 1 Cor. 7.4. The wife hath not the power of her owne body, but the Husband: and likewise also the husband hath not the power of his owne body, but the wife: and by the law of Moses, both the adulterer and the adulteresse were equally punishable, and were both to be put to death. Job. 31.9.10. Iob saith if he had beene an adulterer, then let his wife become an adulteresse. It seemes therefore if the hus∣band commit adultery, then his wife may doe the like and be excusable, and that she may doe it as a iust reward of his vn∣faithfullnesse towards her. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the Lord may and dth many times, in his iust iudgement punish sinne with sinne, and that in the same kinde; as the adultery of the husband with the adultery of the wife, and the adultery of the wife with the adultery of the husband; and that is Iobs meaning, that the Lord might so haue punished him, if he had beene vnfaithfull to his wife: but neither may the wife purposely become an adulteresse, because her husband is an adulterer, nor the husband purpose∣ly
become an adulterer because his wife is an adulteresse, they may not take on them so to punish the sinne one of the other. Quest. When is any act of vncleannesse and fleshly defilement which is naturall and according to the course of nature corrupted, in any kind; whether incest, fornication or adultery, most vile and odious?Gen. 34.2. Deut. 22.25. 2. Sam. 13.14. Answ. When it is committed by violence and force, which is called rape, as it is thought that was of Shechem. Gen 34.2. Quest. How is chastitie hurt or hindered in man or woman, with many others? Answ. Two wayes. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. This;Leuit. 19.29. Deut. 23.17. Ezech. 16.28.29. by vncleannesse and defilement of the bo∣dy, committed by man or by woman, with many others at large; as when a man commits filthinesse with many women whatsoeuer they be:Hosea 4.2. or when a woman doth prostitute her body to many men, and commits filthinesse with many men whatsoeuer they be. Quest. What is the second way by which chastitie is hurt or hindered in man or woman with many others? Answ. This;Gen. 2.24. Deut. 17.17. Mth. 19.5. Leuit. 18.18. Math. 2.15. 1 Cor. 7.2. by vncleannesse and defilement of the bo∣dy, committed by man or woman with many others to whom they seeme to be bound by the bond of marriage: as when a man hath more then one wife at one and the same time, and hath carnall copulation with them, or when a woman hath more then an husband at one and the same time and hath car∣nall copulation with them. Gen. 16.2.3. Abraham had more then one wife at one and the same time. And (Gen. 29.28) so had Jacob. 1 Sam. 1.2. El∣kanah. 1 Sam. 25.42.43. Dauid and many other holy men, had more then one wife at one and the same time: therefore it seemes lawfull for a man to haue more then one wife, at one and the same time. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; though the Lord hauing promised to make Abrahams seede as the Stars of Heauen, & as the sand of the sea shore. Gen. 22.17. was pleased to suffer variety of wiues for a time, as a meanes to increase that posterity, and so it was in some sort excusable; yet it was a fault and a fayling in the Patriarkes, and in holy men of old, and cannot bee
iustifyed and defended as a thing lawfull and void of sinne. After lawfull diuorce for Adulterie, the partie innocent hauing not the gift of continency, on leaue obtained of the Church and christian Magistrate, may lawfully marry ano∣ther; and so it will come to passe that the husband shall haue two wiues both liuing at one time, or the wife shall haue two husbands both liuing at one time. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; neither the husband being the party inno∣cent, and marrying another after lawfull diuorce, hath two wiues both liuing at one and the same time: nor the wife being the party innocent and marrying another after lawfull diuorce hath two husbands both liuing at one and the same time: for after lawfull diuorce, the parties diuorced are not man and wife: the bond of marriage is quite broken. The Papists obiect Rom 7.2.3. A wife is bound to her hus∣band while he liueth, and if the man be dead then she is at libertie: therefore say they nothing but death dissolues the bond of Marriage. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the Apostle there hauing no occasion to entreate of diuorce, speakes of marriage as it stands whole and sound by Gods Ordinance, that by the Ordinance of God, marriage continuing vndissolued till death, the woman is bound to her husband so long as he liueth: and therefore he saith not that nothing dissolues the bond of marriage but death: but though the bond hold during life, yet by death it is dissolued: that is his meaning. 1 Cor. 7.10.11. Let not the wife depart from her husband, but if she depart let her remaine vnmarried: therefore say they after lawfull diuorce, the parties diuorced are man and wife still, and the innocent partie may not marry with another. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the Apostle there speakes not of diuorce for Adultery, but of other seperations caused by dissentions in marriage: and they that seperate hereupon ought not to mar∣rie: and therefore he saith if she dpart, let her remaine vn∣married, not if she be put away, and let her not depart as be∣ing
in her owne choyce whether to depart or no: now in the case of diuorce for adultery, shee is to depart whether shee will or no. Now to the Affirmatiue part of the seuenth Com∣mandement. Quest. What doth the seuenth Commandement require? Answ. In generall two things. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; Chastitie both inward and outward, which is cleannesse and puritie both of the soule and of the body of man or woman, touching the matter of generation. Quest. VVherein stands inward chastitie and cleannesse, and puritie of the soule of man or woman touching the matter of ge∣neration? Answ. In a freedome by grace from fleshly concupi∣scence, the heart being by grace freed from filthy, vncleane,Math. 5.28. Math. 15.19. 1 Cor. 7.37. Coloss. 3.5. and vnchast thoughts, and from inward filthy lusts and from purposes and desires to any act of vncleannesse and fleshly defilement. Quest. VVherein stands outward chastitie and cleannesse, and puritie of the body of man or woman, touching the matter of ge∣neration? Answ.Gen. 39.8.9.10.12. 2 Cor. 7.1. 1 Thess. 4 3 4. 1 Tim. 4.12. Tit. 2.. Reuel. 15.4. In not putting in execution the concupiscence of the flesh in any act of vncleannesse and fleshly defilement in any kind whatsoeuer, either with themselues or others, be it with one other, or with many others. Quest. What is the second generall thing the seuenth Comman∣dement requires? Answ. This; a carefull vsing of such things as are helpes to preserue chastitie, and doe tend to the preseruation of clannesse and puritie both inward and outward, both of the soule and of the body of man or woman touching the matter of generation. Quest. VVhat are the things that helpe to preserue chastitie, and doe tend to the preseruation of cleannesse and puritie both of the soule and of the body of man or woman, touching the matter of generation? Answ. Seuen things especially.
Quest. What is the first of those? Gen. 20.11. Gen. 39.9. Eccles. 7.28.Answ. This; the feare of God in respect of his word and Commandement, that forbids vncleannesse and fleshly de∣filement, both of soule and body in any kind whatsoeuer. Quest. What is the second thing that helps to preserue chastity, and tends to the preseruation of cleannesse and puritie, both of the soule and of the body of man or woman, touching the matter of generation? Psal. 119.9.Answ. This; a true delight in the word of God, and in his holy ordinances. Prou. 2.10.16. compared with Pro. 5.1.2.3 Pro.. 20, 621, 23, 24. Quest. What is the third thing that helps to preserues chastity, and tends to the preseruation of cleanness & purity both of the soule and the body of man or woman, touching the matter of generation? Answ. This; modesty or shamefac'tnesse, which is an ho∣ly abhorring of all filthinesse and fleshly defilement,Ephes. 5.3.4. accom∣panied with a carefull obseruing of Christian comlinesse, and with a certaine griefe and feare, least any thing vncome∣ly should be committed. Quest. VVherein is modestie or shamefac'tnes to bee expressed, and to appeare? Answ. In three things especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Gen. 4.1. Psal. 51. title. Pro. 10.19. Pro. 7.11.Answ. This; in speech and in words, men and women are to expresse their modestie in decent talk and chaste speeches, vsing as seemely words as may bee chosen, when they are to mention things that may moue blushing, and vsing little and submisse speech. Quest. What is the second thing wherein modesty or shame∣fac'tnesse is to be expressed and to appeare? Answ. In countenance and in gesture, and in carriage of the body and outward behauiour,Gen. 24.65. Iob. 31.1. Pro. 6.25. Pro. 7.13. Ierem. 3.3. Tit. 2.3.7. men and women are to ex∣presse their modesty in so looking & so carrying their eyes & countenances as that they neither thereby expresse the filthy lust of their owne hearts, nor giue iust occasion to stirre vp the concupiscence of the heart in others: and in grauitie of their carriage and outward behauiour. Quest. What is the third thing wherein modestie or shame∣fac'tnesse
is to bee expressed and to appeare? Answ. In apparell:1 Tim. 2.9.10. 1 Pet. 3.3.4. men and women are to couer their bo∣dies with decent and comely apparell, and so to attire them∣selues, as that in their apparell they doe expresse the vertues of their minds, and the graces that be in their hearts, especi∣ally modesty, shamefc'tanesse, & frugalitie. Quest. Wherein stands decency and comlinesse of apparell? Answ. In two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; in couering the whole body with it,Gen. 3.10.21. Deut. 28.48. Ezech. 16.7. some parts excepted: men and women are to couer their whole bo∣dies with apparell, leauing onely their hands and faces o∣pen and bare for necessitie sake, Gen. 3.10, 21. By sinne came shame on the whole body, and the Lord made and appoyn∣ted the wearing of garments for the couering of the defor∣mitie of our naked bodies. Deuter. 28.48. Nakednesse is a cuse: therefore affected nakednesse is monstrous and most vile. Quest. What is the second thing wherein stands decency and comlinesse of apparell? Answ.Deut. 22.5 Mat. 11.8. Zeph. 11.8 1 Cor. 11.16. Philip. 4.8. 1 Pet. 3.5 In being decent and comely for the forme and fa∣shion of it, which is when it is according to the sex, and ac∣cording to the office and calling and to the order and degree that men or women are in the societies of men publike or priuate, and according to their ability, & framed according to the ancient custome of the place and country where they liue, and to the example of the grauest and of the most godly and sober men and women of their order and place. Qust. May not men and women vse ornaments of gold, siluer, precious stones, silkes, veluets, laces, and the like? Answ. Yes, they may;Gen. 24.22.47: Gen. 41.42. Exod 2 some necessary cautions in vsing of them being duly obserued. Psal. 45.13, 14. Mat. 6.29. Isa. 18 19, 20, 21, 22, 23, 24. ver. The Prophet condemnes in particular certaine ornaments of bracelets, tires of the head, eare-rings, rings, and diuers other ornaments; and therefore it seemes altogether vnlawfull to vse such particular orna∣ments, or the like. Quest. How is this to bee answered?
Answ. Thus; some ornaments there reckoned vp by the Prophet were indeed meere vanities, and should not haue bin vsed at all; but other particulars were in themselues lawfull, and the Prophet did not simply condemne but onely the abuse of them, in that they were made instruments and signes of the pride, wantonnesse, vanitie and lightnesse of the women of Ierusalem, as appeares ver. 16. 1 Tim. 2.9. and 1 Pet. 3.3. The Apostle forbids wearing of gold and costly apparell, therefore it seemes vnlawfull to vse ornaments of gold, siluer, precious stones, silkes, veluets, la∣ces, and the like. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; the Apostles in those places doe not simply forbid ornaments of gold, siluer, precious stones, silkes, vel∣vets, laces, and such like, but the abuse of them in riot and excesse, directing their speeches to women, who in all likeli∣hood were excessiue in outward adorning and trimming of their bodies, and accounted outward ornaments of golde, pearle, siluer, and such like, their chiefe ornaments, and so neglected modestie and humilitie, the chiefe ornaments of Christians: therefore Paul saith, Let them array themselues in comely apparell, with shamefac'tnesse and modestie, not with broy∣dered hayre, or gold, or pearle, or costly apparell. And Peter saith, Whose apparelling let it not be outward with broydered hayre, and gold put about, or in putting on of apparell; ver. 4. but let the hid man of the heart be vncorrupt with a meeke and quiet spirit, which is before God a thing much set by. Quest. What are the necessary cautions to be obserued in vsing ornaments of golde, siluer, precious stones, silke, veluet, laces, and the like? Answ. They are three especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; that they bee vsed sparingly, and with moderation,Dan. 5.16.17.29. compared. Math. 11.8. and according to the place and calling, order and degree of men and women, and according to the exam∣ple of the grauest and most godly and religious of their place, order, degree and age. Quest. What is the second necessary caution to bee obserued in
vsing ornaments of gold, siluer, precious stones, silkes, veluets, la∣ces, and the like? Answ. This; that they be vsed not alwayes alike,Iere. 2.23. Luk. 16.19. but ac∣cording to the times and seasons. Quest. VVhat is the third necessary caution to bee obserued in vsing ornaments of golde, siluer, precious stones, silkes, veluets, la∣ces, and the like? Answ. This; that they bee vsed to a right end,Gen. 24.15. Pro. 7.10.16. 1 Cor. 12.2 1 Thess. 4.4. not to the gaining of praise amongst men, or to the getting of a name of ric and great persons, to the purchasing of loue from stranger (as harlots doe) but onely to the honouring of the body, tha therein God may be honoured, and not with any delight in them otherwise. Gen. 24.15. the simplicity of that age is to be considered, they did not set teir delight on out∣ward ornaments. Prou. 7.10.16. The harlots practice. Quest What is the fourth thing that helpes to preserue cha∣stitie, and tends to the preseruation of cleannesse and puritie both of the soule and body of man or woman, touching the matter of ge∣neration? Answ. This; temperance or sobrietie,Gal. 5.13. 1 Tim 3.2. Tit. 1.8. Tit. 2.12  Pet. 1.6. which is a moderate and sober vse of such things as belong to the body, agreeable to the time, place, and persons. Quest. Wherein is temperance and sobrietie to bee exercised and expressed? Answ. In three things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This, in dyet:Pro. 23.29. to 33. Ecles. 10.17. Luk 21.34. Ephes. 5 18. 1 Cor. 9.27. 2 Cor. 6.6. men and women are to exercise tem∣perance and sobrietie in their eating and drinking, vsing meats and drinkes onely so farre forth as they may serue to refresh nature, and to make them fit for the seruice of God and man; and sometimes in conuenient abstinence, abstai∣ning from the necessary and ordinary food of their bodies for a time, as need doth require, and as their strength may beare, without abolishing and destroying nature. Quest. VVhat is the second thing wherein temperance and so∣brietie is to be exercised and expressed? Answ. This, in sleepe: men and women are to exercise temperance and sobrietie in their sleeping, onely taking so
much sleepe as may make them better able to doe all good duties that concerne them towards God and man,ro. 20.13. Cor. 6.6. Cor. 11.27. sometimes refraining from sleepe, and watching as need requires, and as they are able: so as it be not to the destruction of na∣ture. Quest. What is the third thing wherein temperance and so∣brietie is to be exercised and expressed? Rom. 13.14: Cor. 7.29.30. Galat. 5.13.Answ. This; in lawfull pleasure and honest delights, men and women are to exercise temperance and sobritie in their lawfull pleasures and honest delights, vsing them onely so farre forth as they bee no prouocations to flshly lustes, nor hinderances to them in good duties towards God or man. Quest. VVhat is the fift thing that helpes to preserue cha∣stitie, and tends to the preseruation of cleannesse and puritie both of the soule and body of man or woman, touching the matter of generation?
