Dan. 4.24 Michah. 6.10. a man or a woman must make recompence and satisfaction to another or others, one or more: for whatso∣euer their consciences charge them, that they haue vniustly gotten or detayned from them: as, for things they haue got∣ten from them by vsurie, by violence, by secret stealth, or by fraud or the like: or for things that haue beene lent to them or left with them in trust: or the things they haue found, or the like, which they haue vniustly with hold from them. Quest. How is a man or a woman to make recompence and satisfaction to another or others one or more, for things they haue vniustly gotten or detained from them? Answ. Thus;Leuit. 6.2.3.4.5 Num. 5.6.7. 2 Sam. 12.6. Luk. 19.8. by returning to them either the same things euery way as good as they were when they first had them, with an ouerplus answerable to the dammage they haue by the want of them: or else things of the same kinde euery way as good as they were, both for quantity and for the worth and value of them, with so much ouer and aboue, as they haue sustained losse or hinderance by the want of them for the time they haue wanted them. Quest. What if goods vniustly gotten or detained, be for their quantity or value vnknowne: how is then recompence and satis∣faction to be made? Answ. Recompence and satisfaction must then be made according to their owne iudgement,Pro 6.31. Luk. 19.8. who haue vniustly got∣ten or detained them: and according to the iudgement and discretion of others, that are wise and conscionable, and that with the most as it shall be thought fit. Quest. What if the partie or parties, from whom goods haue beene vniustly gotten or detained, be either dead or vnknowne, how is then recompence and satisfaction to be made? Answ. If the partie or parties be dead, then recompence must be made to their children if they haue any;Nomb. 5.8. Dan: 4.24. Luk: 19.8. if they haue none, then to the next of their kindred; or if none can bee found, then to the Church or to the poore: and if the partie or parties from whom the goods haue beene vniustly gotten or taken, be vnknowne, then recompence or satisfaction
must be made to the Church, or to the poore. Question. What if a man or a woman that should make re∣compence and satisfaction for goods vniustly gotten and detayned, be not able to doe it, and haue not wherewithall, what are they then to doe? Answ. They must then shew themselues willing and ready to doe it, by a plaine and full confession of their fault, and by crauing pardon for it, with a full purpose, if euer God make them able to make full recompence and satisfaction, for in this case that holds good. 2 Cor. 8.12.2 Cor. 8.12. Quest. What if the partie or parties, from whom goods haue beene vniustly gotten or detained, on the discouery of the wrong done to them, will take aduantage to vse extreamity against him or her that hath done the wrong, what is then to be done? Answ. In this case it is the iudgement of the best Di∣uines, that a third person, one that is of good accoumpt for wisedome, Religion, and honestie is to bee chosen, to whom the secret may safely be reuealed, and hee is to bee intreated to deale betweene them, and to conuey to the partie or par∣ties wronged so much, as will answer their losse and dam∣mage in the behalfe of the partie that hath offended, concea∣ling his or her name and the particular fault, entreating not to enquire after it, and to rest satisfied with that is brought to them. Now to the ninth Commandement. Exodus. 20.16. Thou shalt not beare false witnesse against thy Neighbour. Quest. What reasons may be giuen touching the order of this Commandement, that forbids false witnesse bearing? Answ. Two especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; witnesse bearing is commonly in matters of controuersie touching goods, that there be no vniust getting of them, either in matter of contract or out of contract, or a∣ny other way which was forbidden in the former Comman∣mandement, and therefore this Commandement followes fitly on the former.
Quest. What is the second reason touching the order of this commandement, that forbids false witnesse bearing? Answ. This; in the fifth commandement the Magistrates duty is commanded, and in the three next commandements, Thou shalt not kill. Thou shalt not steale: Such sinnes are fore∣bidden as, being knowne,Rom. 13.4. Deut. 19.15. are to bee punished by the Magi∣strate, he being set for the punishment of the wicked, and for the defence of the godly: and that the Magistrat may punish offenders and breakers of those commandements, according to the truth, he must doe it by witnesse: and therefore this commandement touching true witnesse bearing, and auoy∣ding of false witnesse, followes fitly on the former. Quest. What are the words of the ninth Commandement? Answ. Those wee finde Exod. 20.16. Thou shalt not beare false witnesse against thy Neighbour. Quest. What is here meant when the Lord saith, Thou shalt not beare false witnesse? Answ. The words doe properly signifie, thou shalt not answer false witnesse against thy neighbour; in speciall, thou shalt not answer falsely in publike before a Magistrate: the word (answere) is sometimes in Scripture vsed in a more ge∣nerall for the word speake, as Math. 11.25. and so it is here to be taken, as if it had beene said, thou shalt not speake any thing, whereby thou maist hurt the good name and credit of thy neighbour. Quest. What are we here to vnderstand by the word Neigh∣bour? Answ. Not onely one that is nere to vs in place and habi∣tation,Isai. 58.7. Luk. 10.36.37. or one to whom we are knit in speciall manner by the bond of nature, or some other speciall bond, but any one who∣soeuer that is of the same flesh, of the same nature with vs, any man or woman whatsoeuer. Quest. What is the ground of this prohibition, thou shalt not speake any thing whereby thou maist hurt the good name and credit of any one that is of the same flesh, of the same nature with thee? Answ. This; both the maintenance and preseruation of truth amongst men,Deut. 32.4. Tit. 1.2. which makes much both for the glory of God, who is Truth it selfe, Deut. 32.4. And also for the good
of men, for all vse of speech of man to man depends on the truth of it;Iosh. 7.19. Zach. 8.16. Ephes. 4 25. Pro. 22.1. without truth in our speeches, humane societies and dealings betweene man and man cannot be maintained, and also the maintenance of the good name both of our selues and others, which is better then riches. Quest. What is the summe of this Commandement? Mat. 7.1. Philip 4.8. 1 Cor. 13.5.Answ. That the good name, credit, and estimation, either of our selues or others, be not any way hurt or hindered, but that it be by all good meanes maintained and preserued. Now this Commandement being Negatiue, I will first shew what it forbids. Quest. What doth this Commandement forbid? Answ. In generall, whatsoeuer is contrary to the truth, and tends to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of man or woman. Quest. What are the things that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of man or woman? Answ. Either such things as are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of a man or a womans owne good name; or such things as are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good ame of another, or others one or more. Quest. What are the things that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of a man or a womans good name? Answ. They are either things inward in the heart, or things expressed and vttered by the tongue. Quest. What are the things inward in the heart, that are con∣trary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of a man or womans owne good name? Answ. Two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; selfe conceitednesse and an ouerweening of their owne excellency:Pro. 26.12. Luk. 18.11. Act. 12.22.23. 1 Cor. 8.1.2. when a man or a woman doe thinke themselues either to be that which they are not, or to haue that in them which they haue not: or are too highly concei∣ted of the good things they haue, and in their owne swelling
conceit doe magnifie themselues in regard of their owne good gifts aboue others,Galat. 6.3. Philip. 2.3. and thinke basely of others in com∣parison of themselues. Quest. What is the second thing inward in the heart that is contrary to the truth, and tends to the hurt or hinderance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. This; too base and too meane a conceit and an vn∣derweening of the good things that be in themselues; when a man or a woman doe thinke that either they haue not that grace, and those good things, or not that measure of grace and of good things that indeed they haue. Thus sometimes doe sound and true hearted Christians in time of tentation, if they haue lost their feeling for a while, and cannot finde that reioycing in God and in good things they were wont, they thinke themselues to be but hypocrites, and that they haue no true grace in them at all, and so they beare false witnesse a∣gainst themselues. Iob 27.5, 6.Iob. 27.5.6. Iob would not so doe. Psal. 7.8.Psal. 7.8. in causa particulari, &c. 2 Cor. 1.12.2 Cor 1.12. 1 Cor. 4.3. I iudge not mine owne selfe. A man or a woman cannot certainly and truely iudge of themselues and of their owne goodnesse: and therefore they cannot but either ouer or vnderweene the good things that be in themselues. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the meaning of that place is, that the Apo∣stle rested not in the iudgement of his owne conscience tou∣ching himselfe, and his faithfulnesse in his office and calling, as the highest iudgement, and as sufficient to cleare him be∣fore the Iudgement seate of God: his Conscience was able, and did certainly and truely witnesse to himselfe his faithful∣nesse in his calling, but he durst not rest in that as sufficient to cleare him, and to iustifie him before the Iudgement seate of God, the Lord could find matter enough against him to condemne him notwithstanding that. Iob 4.18. And therfore that place proues not that a man or woman cannot certainly and truely iudge of themselues, and of their owne goodnes, and so cannot but either ouerweene or vnderweene the good things that be in themselues. Quest. What are the things expressed & vttered by the tongue,
that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. Three things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Pro. 27.2. Isai. 65.5. Mat. 19.20. Act: 8.6. Rom. 1.30.Answ. This; vain-glorious boasting and bragging, when a man or woman doe speake great things of themselues, to get them praise and commendation amongst others; and doe say that either they are that which they are not, or haue that goodnesse in them which they haue not, or haue done this or that good; or that others by their meanes haue done this or that good, when there is no such matter. Quest. What is the worst kind of boasting and bragging, and when is boasting most vile and odious? Psal. 52.1. Isai. 66.5. Ierem. 7.9.10.Answ. A boasting of wickednesse and sinne, when a man or woman do boast and brag of the euill and wickednes they haue done, or are able to doe, as of matter worthy praise and commendation. Quest. Is all boasting vnlawfull, and may not a man or wo∣man sometimes speake of the good things that bee in themselues, or of the good they haue done, to their owne praise & commendation? Answ. There is sometimes a necessary and lawfull kind of boasting; a boasting which may and ought to be vsed: as when a man or woman is disgraced, and their disgrace tends to the dishonour of God, and to the disgrace of the Gospell, and of Religion, they may then boast of the good things that are in them, or of the good they haue done, so as it be in an holy manner, with a due acknowledgement of Gods grace with modestie, and without disgrace to any. Thus the Apostle was forced to boast, 2 Cor. 11.16, 17, 21, 22, 23, &c. Galat. 2.6, 7, 8. Quest. What is the second thing expressed and vttered by the tongue contrary to the truth, that tends to the hurt or hinderance of a man or a womans owne good name? Gen. 3.12.13. 1 Sam. 13.11.12.13. 1 Sam. 15.15.21 Luk. 14.18.19.20.Answ. This; the lessening and extenuating of their faults, when a man or woman by speech extenuate, and lessen, and seeke to excuse themselues for the faults they are guiltie of, and are iustly charged withall. Quest. Is it altogether vnlawfull for a man or woman to ex∣cuse
themselues for the things done by them, which are charged on them as faults? Answ. It is altogether vnlawfull for a man or woman to excuse themselues for things done by them, which are char∣ged on them, as faults being euill and sinnefull, so farre as they are euill and sinnefull: but for the things done by them, which are charged on them as faults being not e∣uill and sinnefull, they may lawfully excuse themselues. Thus did Reuben, Gad, and halfe the Tribe of Ma∣nasseh, Ioshua 22.22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28, 29, 30. Thus did Dauid, 1. Sam. 17.29. 1. Sam. 22.14, 15. Math. 12.3, 4, 5, &c. Quest. What is the third thing expressed and vttered by the tongue contrary to the truth, that tends to the hurt or hinderance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. This; vniust accusing of themselues,Pro. 13.7. Isai. 56.3. when a man or woman doe by speach either denie or extenuate and lessen the graces and gifts God hath bestowed on them, and say contrarie to that which they knowe and thinke in a kinde of proud humilitie, they haue now it nor wealth, and they are not able to doe this or that good thing. Quest. What are the things that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. They are either things inward in the heart, or things expressed and vttered by the tongue. Quest. What are the things inward in the heart that are con∣trary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. Foure things especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. This; light and wrongfull suspition,Iudg. 15.2. 1 Sam. 1.13. 2 Sam. 10.3. Ierem. 43.3. Luk. 7 39. Act. 28.4. 1 Tm. 6.4. and euill sur∣mising, when a man or woman doe causelessely misdeeme of another or others, one or more, and within themselues con∣clude, that they are guiltie of some euill, and doe surmise and suspect some euill by them without any euident or sufficient cause or ground.
Quest. May a man or woman then sometimes lawfully and iustly suspect euill by another or others, one or more? Answ. Yes, they may, if the suspition arise on a probable and sufficient cause, and the thing suspcted bee not certainly concluded, but left in suspence and doubt; and if the suspition be to a good end, as to beware of the partie suspected, and of his euill, then it is lawfull and iust. Thus did Abraham, Gen. 20.11.Gen. 20.11. Gedaliah the sonne of Ahikam was too blame, that hee would not suspct bloody. Ishmael, that was sent to kill him. Ierem. 40.16. & 41.12,Ierem. 40.16. Ierem. 41.12. &c. Math. 10.17.Mat. 10.17. It is the rule that Christ giues, that we should suspect euill men, and take heed of them. Quest. Whence comes it that men or women doe causelesly su∣spect euill of another or others, one or more? Answ. Either from their weaknesse of iudgement, or from their owne guiltinesse of sinne,Act. 28.4. 1 Sam. 24.10. 1 Cor. 13.7. or from some ill affection: men or women doe causelesly suspect euill of others, either be∣cause they want sound & good iudgement, or because them∣selues are wicked and guiltie of foule sinnes, or because they are ill affected, and their hearts are taken vp with enuie or hatred against them whom they suspect. Acts 28.4. The Bar∣barians were weake in iudgement. 1 Sam. 24.10. Saul was suspicious of Dauid, because hee had deserued euill of him. 1 Cor. 13.7. Loue couereth all things, and want of loue is the cause of euill suspition. Quest. What is the second thing inward in the heart, that is contrary to the truth, and tends to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Mat. 7.1. Rom: 2.1. Rom. 14.3.4.10.Answ. This; rash, vncharitable, and vniust iudging and condemning of another or others, one or more; when a man or a woman in their hearts doe rashly, vncharitably and vn∣iustly iudge and condemne another or others, one or more, and thinke disgracefully of them Quest. How doe men or women in their hearts rashly, vn∣charitably, and vniustly iudge and condemne another or others, one or more, and thinke disgracefully of them? Answ. Two wayes; either in respect of their persons, or in regard of thir words and deeds.
Quest. How doe men or women in their hearts rashly, vncha∣ritably and vniustly iudge, and condemne another or others, one or more, and thinke disgracefully of them in respect of their persons? Answ. Thus; when they thinke otherwise of their persons then they ought to doe, in regard of some slips, infirmities, euill reports; or in regard of some crosses, or some strange ac∣cident that befalls them. Thus Iobs friends iudged him an hy∣pocrite, Iob. 4.5.8. Psal. 41.1. Luke 13 2, 3, 4, 5. Quest. How doe men or women in their hearts rashly, vncha∣ritably, and vniustly iudge and condemne another or others, one or more, and thinke disgracefully of them in regard of their words or deedes? Answ. Thus; when they think or iudge otherwise of their words or deeds then they ought to doe: as when they either thinke and iudge ill of the good speeches or actions of o∣thers. Thus doe wicked men of the good speeches and acti∣ons of Gods children,Act. 2.13.15. 2 Sam. 10.3. 2 King. 5.7. Isai. 11.3. Rom. 1.29. or doe take their speeches or actions that are indifferent, in the worst part, or doe think and iudge things that are spoken or done amisse by them, worse then they are; and doe think a light and a small offence, and a little failing in their speech or behauiour, to be a great offence, and more foule and griuous then it is; when Christ spake com∣fortably to the sicke of the palsie, Mat. 9.2. the Scribes and Pharisies said he blasphemeth, ver. 3. Quest. What is the third thing inward in the heart that is con∣trary to the truth, and tends to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. This; inward contemning, and thinking basely of another or others, one or more, and disdaining of them; Sam. 6.16. Isai. 53.2.3. Mat. 18.10. when a man or woman do carry in themselues base, contemptuous, and disdainefull thoughts of others, and doe in their hearts despise them for worldly respects, as because they are poore, or of meane callings, or deformed in body, or of meane gifts, or in great distresse, or the like. Psal. 15.4. It is a note of one that shall dwell in the Lords Tabernacle, and rest in his holy Mountaine, that hee contem∣neth a vile person: It seemes therefore that a man or woman
may lawfully in their hearts contemne others that are base and vile. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; the meaning of that place is, that Gods children may and ought in their hearts to contemne such as are vile and base sinners in whom sinne reigneth, and who commit sinne with greedinesse, and are to euery good worke reprobate, though they be great or wealthy in the world, in regard of their wickednes and sin. Thus Antiochus Epiphanes Dan. 11.21.Dan. 11.21. is called a vile person. And the Lord saith, 1 Sam. 2.30.1 Sam. 2.30. They that despise me, shall be despised: and so that place prooues not that a man or woman may in their hearts con∣temne others that are base in worldly respects. What if notorious wicked men bee Magistrates and Go∣uernours? Quest. May we then contemne them in our hearts? Answ. As they be wicked men, and haue altogether defa∣ced the image of God touching holinesse and righteousnesse, they may be contemned; but as they are Magistrates or go∣uernors, they beare before vs the image of Gods power and authoritie▪ and in that respect honour and obedience is due vnto them in the Lord. Quest. What is the fourth thing inward in the heart that is contrary to the truth, and tends to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? 2 Cor. 12.6. Iud. vers: 16.Ans. This; admiring of others, and magnifying of them in the inward conceit of the heart aboue their worth. When a man or a woman do admire and thinke more highly either of the persons of others, or of their gifts or of the things done by them, then there is iust cause, and then they ought. Quest. VVhen is vniust admiring of others, and magnifying of them in the inward conceit of the heart most vile and most odious? Act. 8.10.11. Act. 20.30. 2 Cor. 11.20. Psal. 49.18.Answ. When men or women do admire another or others, one or more, and do magnifie them in the inward conceit of their hearts for their errors and sinnes. Thus do seduced per∣sons admire and magnifie their false teachers and seducers; and thus also doe some admire others for their sinnes.
Quest. What are the things expressed and vttered by the tongue that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hin∣derance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. Either things expressed and vttered to another or others one or more, or things expressed and vttered of ano∣ther or others, one or more. Quest. What are the things expressed and vttered to another or others, one or more, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. Either things vttered vainely, or things vttered falsely. Quest. What are the things vttered to another or others, one or more, vainly, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. They are things vttered without reason,1 Tim. 5.13. 2 Sam. 17.18. Pro. 10.19. Iam. 1.19. and out of season: when a man or woman are pratlers, and too full of words, and do keepe nothing secret, but tell whatsoeuer they know, and doe needlessely publish the secrets or infirmities of others to their discredit. Quest. VVhat are the things vttered to another or others, one or more falsely, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ: Two things especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. This, lying:Exod. 23.7. Leuit. 19.11. Psal. 101.7. Pro. 12.22. Ephes. 4.22. Coloss. 3.9. 2 King. 5.25. Gen. 3.45. Ioh. 8.44. Ierem. 5.31. Ierem. 23.25.26.32. 1 Tim. 4.2. when a man or woman doe wittingly and willingly speake that which they know is false, with a mind and purpose to deceiue. Quest. What is the worst kinde of lying, and when is lying most foule and most odious? Answ. When it is either to cloke and smother ouer a sinne already committed, or to make way for sinne, and the doing of some euill, or when it is to hurt or to intrap another or o∣thers, one or more, and to draw them into some errour or sin, or into some danger. Quest. May not a man or a woman sometimes in speaking wit∣tingly and willingly, put one word, or one thing for another?
Answ. Yes, they may and not lye, as they may sometimes vse Metaphors, and other figuratiue speeches to expresse the truth more significantly;Iudg. 9.8.9. 2 Sam. 12.12. &c. 2 King. 14.9. Mat: 21.33. to 42. or they may somtimes vtter a thing supposed or fayned, a parable to lay forth the truth more profitably, that the truth may bee more clearely discerned, and more sincerely acknowledged: or they may sometimes speake something not contrary, but besides, or diuers from the truth, and yet not lye; as when parents who would in∣sinuate to their little children the dangers of some pit or ditch, they say to them, Take heed, there is a Beare, or a Bull-beggar. What if our owne life, or the life of another or others, one or more be endangered, and may be redeemed by vsing a lye? Quest. Is it not lawfull in that case to lye? Rom: 3.8.Answ. No, it is not, lying being in it owne nature simply euill, it may not bee vsed for the sauing either of our owne life, or the life of any other. Of two euils the lesse is to be chosen. Now it may so fall out, that a lye may bee a lesse euill, then that which may fol∣low on the telling of it: for example, It may bee that a man by telling of a lye may keepe close an innocent person, that lyes hid from another who seekes his life, and intends to kill him; and by saying hee knowes not where he is, though he doe know, hee may hinder the one from murdering, and the other from being murdered. It seemes that in this case a lye may be admitted. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; that rule of two euils, the lesse is to be cho∣sen, is to be vnderstood of such euills as are punishments, or inconueniences, not of such euills as are sinnes; no euill of sinne is is to be admitted at all, neither will it stand good in the sight of God to escape a greater sinne by committing a lesser. And in the case propounded, a man may auoyd both lying, and also the discouering of him that lies hid: for hee may either be silent, or say, he knowes where he is, but he will not discouer him: & this he is rather to doe, then to lye, or to discouer him, though he do therby expose himselfe to danger, through the rage of him that pursues the innocent partie.
It may be that a lie may further the saluation of another, as it may haply serue to discouer an heretike, and to reclaime him from his heresie; or it may serue to bring an heathen man from Paganisme to Christianitie. Quest. May it not bee lawfull in that case to lie? Answ. No, it is not lawfull to lye for the saluation of men;Iob 13.7. 1 Cor. 15.15. God will not haue vs to lye for his cause, much lesse may wee lye for the best good of men. Ephes. 4 25. Christians are to cast off lying, and to speake the truth one to another, because they are members one of another: therefore it seemes that Christians may lawfully lye to Infi∣dels, and to such as professe not the same truth with them, for they are not members one of another. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the Apostles reason there must be conceiued, as binding beleeuers and professors of the Gospell more strictly to speake the truth one to another, and not to lye one to another, because being members of the same body, its more grieuous for them to lye one to another, then to lye to others: but it followes not that therfore they haue libertie to lye to Infidels, & to such as differ from them in Religion, lying be∣ing euill and sinfull to whomsoeuer it be. Gen. 20.2. Abraham said, that his wife Sarah was his sister: and Gen. 26.7. Isaac said of his wife, that shee was his sister: therefore it seemes lawfull sometimes to lye. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; Abraham vttered no vntruth, but only con∣cealed part of the truth, as appeares ver. 12. Againe, the lies of holy men are recorded in Scripture, not with approbation, and for our imitation, that we should doe the like, but as their falls & infirmities, and that their faults and slidings might be warnings to vs. The Mid-wiues of Egypt saued the male children aliue, Exod. 1.19. And Rahab saued the Spies, Iosh. 2.5. by lying, and they are commended for so doing: therefore lying is sometimes lawfull. Quest. How is this to be answered? Ans. Thus; the things they did are commended, not their
manner of doing them: the things they did were workes of mercy, and fruits of faith, and the true feare of God; but they failed in the manner of doing of them: and therefore their examples in lying are not to be imitated. How can faith, and the true feare of God, and a manifest sinne stand together? Answ. Faith, and the true feare of God, and continuance in any knowne sinne, cannot stand together; but faith, and the true feare of God, and a manifest sinne of frailtie may well stand together? Quest. May not a man or a woman in speaking to others sometimes suppresse the truth, and conceale it either in whole or in part? Answ. Yes, they may; when the speaking of the truth is vnnecessary, and they are not called to speake it, either in the matter of Religion, or in ciuill causes; and the speaking of it is ioyned with dammage or danger, either of themselues or others, though they may neither deny the truth, nor vtter an vntruth, yet they may thē conceale the truth, either whol∣ly, or in part, Gen. 20.2. Thus was Samuel taught to doe, 1. Sam. 16.2. Hee was by command from the Lord to conceale the principall cause of his comming to Bethlem. Quest. May not a man or a woman being asked a question, make answere to it in words, contrarie to that which they know to bee true, reseruing something in their mindes to make their answere good, and so giue an equiuocating answere: as being asked by one that hath power and authoritie to examine them, Whether they were in such a place, and at such a time? may they not answere, they were not, though they were, reseruing in their minde to tell it to you, or not with their heeles vpward, or the like? Answ. No, they may not; for if they so doe, they invert the order and nature of things, and make falsehood truth, and truth falshood; and they turne affirmatiues into negatiues, and negatiues into affirmatiues; and by this deuice it is all one to say, I was not in such a place, with a mentall reserua∣tion, as to say, I was. And againe, he that truly feares God, he speakes the truth in
his heart, Psal. 15.2 he hath truth both in his heart & mouth. Ierem. 38.26, 27. Ieremiah the Prophet, by the aduice of the King, gaue an equiuocating answer to the Princes, when they asked him of the speech that passed betweene the King and him: and therefore an equiuocating answere may some∣times be giuen. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; Ieremiah did neither lye, nor equiuocate in his answere to the Princes: he told them the truth in part, though not the whole truth, touching the speech that passed betweene the King and him, as appeares, vers. 15, 16. There∣fore his example will not warrant the giuing of an equiuo∣cating answere. 1 Kings 22.15. Michaiah answers King Ahab in words contrary to that which he knew: for he knew the King should perish, yet he bids him Goe vp and prosper, equiuocating with him: therefore it seemes lawfull sometimes to answer by e∣quiuocation, and to giue an equiuocating answere. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; the Prophet spake those words, Goe vp and prosper, according to the meaning of the false Prophets iro∣nically, and in scorne, not with any purpose to deceiue, but in such a sense as was knowne to the King, and the King knew his meaning, and therefore charged him to speake seriously, vers. 16. and so his example will not warrant the giuing of an equiuocating answere. Luke 24.28. Christ going to Emaus, made as though he would haue gone further, and yet did not: and therefore say the Pa∣pists, it is lawfull to equiuocate. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; Christ made as though hee would haue gone further, not with any purpose to deceiue those Dis∣ciples, but to make triall of their humanitie: he meant as hee seemed to goe further, but hee was ouercome by their courteous importunity to yeeld to them, as it followes vers 29. They constrained him to stay with them: he yeelded to the sweet violence of their courteous humanitie, as the An∣gels of God did to the vrgent request of Lot, Genes. 19.3.
Therefore this act of Christ proues not the lawfulnesse of an equiuocating answere. iection.Iohn 7.8. Christ said to his brethren, I will not goe vp to the Feast at Ierusalem, meaning (as Bellarmine expoundeth it) not as the Mssiah, but in secret, or not with them, and yet after∣ward he went, ver. 10. therefore (say the Papists) it is lawfull to giue an equiuocating answer. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; Christ there speaketh plainly as he meant: for he said, he would not goe vp yet, or now, because his time was not come: and though he went vp not long after, yet his first saying did stand: for that (yet) was not then come, Iohn 2.4. Though Christ would not shew a miracle to turne water into wine at his mothers bidding, saying, Mine houre is not yet come; yet ere the Feast was finished he did it: they might as well say, that Christ did there equiuocate with his mother; and therefore that place proues not, that an equiuocating answer is to be giuen. Quest. VVhat is the second thing vttered to an other or o∣thers, one or more, falsely and contrary to the truth, that tends to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Prou. 27.14. Math. 22.16. Acts 12.22. Acts 24.2.3.Ans. Such speech as setteth either praise or dispraise where it should not; when a man or woman doe either prais or dis∣praise another or others, one or more, to their faces vniustly. Quest. How doth a man or woman praise another or others, one or more, to their faces vniustly? Answ. By flattering of them; when a man or woman in their words and speech vttered to another o others, one or more, do to their faces praise, commend, & extoll, either their persons or their gifts, or their actions aboue that which they know or thinke, either to get fauour with them, or some way or other for their owne aduantage. Quest. Is it alwayes vnlawfull in words and in speech to praise and commend the persons, gifts, or actions of another or others, one or more, to their faces? Answ. No, it is not; it is sometimes fit and expedient in words to praise & to commend the persons, gifts, or actions
of another or others, one or more, if onely due praise and commendation bee giuen,Exod. 39.43. Iosh. 22.1.2.3. Rom. 13.3. and if it bee done to right ends, as either to confirme or encourage them in well doing, or to comfort such as are too much deiected with the sight and conscience of their owne vnworthinesse and sinnes. Quest. When is flattering of another or others, one or more, most vile and most odious? Answ. When it is with hatred and malice in the heart,Psal. 12.2. Psal. 28.3. Psal. 55.21. Mat. 22.16. when a man or woman doe flatter others, and speake faire to them, and commend them to their faces, and yet hate them in their hearts, and speake euill of them behind their backes. Quest. What is the most hurtfull and dangerous kind of flat∣tering? Answ. That which is vsed in things that concerne the state of the soule;Pro. 29.5. Iere. 6.14. Iere. 23.32. Ezech. 13.18. Rom. 16.18. 1 Thess. 2.5. as when men or women doe flatter and sooth vp others in their sinnes, and doe call their vices vertues, and commend them as vertues, especially in publike. Quest. How doth a man or a woman dispraise another or o∣thers, one or more, to their faces vniustly? Answ. Thus; when in their words & speech vttered to an other or others, one or more, they doe contrary to their owne knowledge, and ut of enuy, dispraise and carp either at their prsons, or at their good gifts and graces, or at their good actions, with a purpose either to disgrace, or to discourage them, and doe call good, euill, as Isa. 5.20. Thus dealt Iobs friends with him, as we may read in many Chapters. Iob. 16.20. his friends spake eloquently against him, to haue discouraged him, and to haue brought him to call his vprightnesse into question, which he said, I will neuer take away mine innocencie from my selfe, I will keepe my righteousnesse, and will not forsake it, Job 27.5, 6. Quest. What are the things expressed and vttered by the tongue of another or others, one or more, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more▪ Answ. Either things on the part of the speaker or speakers, one or more, or things on the part of the hearer or hearers, one or more.
Quest. What are the things on the part of the speaker or speakers, one or more, vttered of another or others, one or more, that are con∣trary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. They are speeches vttered of another or others, one or more, either in priuate, or speeches vttered in publike. Quest. VVhat are the speeches that are vttered of another or others, one or more, in priuate, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or o∣thers, one or more? Ans. Speeches vttered either in the presence of the party or parties, one or more, of whom they are spoken; or they are speeches vttered behind their backs, & out of their presence▪ Quest. What are the speeches vttered in the presence of the par∣tie or parties, one or more, of whom they are spoken that are contra∣ry to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of that partie or parties, one or more? Answ. Speeches falsely charging some euill on another or others, one or more, to their faces, either contrary to know∣ledge, or on some light suspition: when a man or woman doe in their speech,Ier. 37.13.14. 1 Pet. 2.12. either contrary to their owne knowledge, or on some light suspition without any euident and sufficient cause or ground, falsely charge another or others, one or more, to their faces, that they haue spoken or done, or were or are about to doe this or that euill. Thus dealt Irijah with Ieremiah, Iere. 37.13, 14. Quest. VVhat are the speeches vttered behinde the backes, and out of the presence of the partie or parties, one or more, of whom they are spoken, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of that partie or parties, one or more? Leuit. 19.16. Pro. 11.13. &c. 20.19. Ezeuh. 22.9. Rom. 1.29.30. 2 Tim 3.3.Answ. Tale-bearing, backe-biting, and slandering spee∣ches, and malicious defamations: as when a man or wo∣man doe either out of their hatred or enuy, maliciously re∣port ill of another or others, one or more, and doe speake of their faults and defects behinde their backes, to such as will giue eare to them. Quest. How many wayes do men or women carry tales, back-bite,
and slander, and maliciously defame another or others, one or more, behind their backes? Answ. Two wayes especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This;Pro. 18.8. Rom. 1.29. 2 Cor. 12.20. by whispering ill of them when they do se∣cretly and closely speake ill of another or others, one or more, and doe make a malicious report of their faults and defects behind their backs, by roūding in the eare or eares of such as will heare them: of such speaks Dauid, Psal. 101.5. Quest. What is the second way by which men or women doe carry tales, back-bite and slander, and maliciously defame another or others, one or more, behind their backes? Answ. By speaking ill of them more openly;Psal. 15 3. Rom. 1.30. 2 Cor. 12.20. as when a man or woman do speak ill of another or others, one or more, and doe make a malicious report of their faults and defects behind their backs: so as two, or three, or many that are to∣gether in a priuate place may heare them; and these are pro∣perly called back-biters. Quest. What are the effects both of whispering ill, and of spea∣king ill more openly of another or others, one or more, behinde their backes? Answ. Not only the hurt of them in their good names,2 Sam. 16.3.4. Pro. 16.28. Pro. 26.20. Ezech. 22.9. but sometimes also in their goods, somtimes in their friends, and somtimes in their liues; & the talebearer & backbiter increa∣seth hatred among enemies, & soweth discord among friends. Quest When is whispering or speaking ill most vile and odious? Ans. When the report of ill that is either whispered or spo∣ken more openly of another or others,Gen. 39.14. 2 Sam. 16.3. Iere. 18.18. Amos. 7.10. 2 Tim. 3.3. 2 Cor. 11.13. one or more behinde their backs, is false, and the man or woman that do make that report, do deuise & faine things which they whisper or speak more openly of them; or when the malicious report of ill that is either whispered or spoken more openly of another or o∣thers, one or more behind their backs, is coloured ouer with faire pretences; as when the whisperer or backbiter saith he is sorry that the party of whō he speaks, hath done such a thing, or is this or that way faulty; or that he speaks not of malice, but of good will; that hee is constrained to speake; that the party to whom the tale is told, must keep it secret, or the like.
Quest. May not a malicious ill report bee made of another or others, one or more, behind their backes, without either whispering ill, or speaking ill more openly by the tongue? Answ. Yes, it may; a man or a woman may make a malici∣ous ill report of another or others, one or more, and may de∣fame them behind their backs by writing, which is called Li∣belling, or a reporting ill by the penne: for that which may not be spoken, may not be written; the tongue and the penne are compared, Psalm. 45.1. My tongue is as the penne of a swift writer. iection.It may be a man or a woman whispering ill, or speaking ill more openly of another or others, one or more, behinde their backs, doe speake nothing but the truth. Quest. May they not so doe? Answ. If they do either whisper ill, or speak ill more open∣ly of another or others,al. 52.2.3.0.10.12. Pet. 4.8. one or more behind their backs, & in so doing do vtter nothing but the truth; yet if they speak that truth out of hatred, and with an intent or a desire to hurt the partie or parties of whom they speake, they are back-biters and slanderers. It was true which Doeg reported of Dauid and Abimelech the Priest, 1. Sam. 22.9, 10. but because his report was out of hatred and to an ill end, hee is accounted a slanderer. Quest. May not a man or a woman then speake of the faults, and of the offences of another or others, one or more, behinde their backes, nor mention them at all? Answ. Yes they may in two cases lawfully. Quest. What is the first of those? Gen. 37.2. Mat. 18.15. 1 Cor. 1.11.Answ. This; if they haue first admonished the partie or parties whose faults and offences they speake of, priuately, and they are not bettered by their priuate admonition, they may then, so as it be in loue, and with a desire of their a∣mendment, speake of those faults and offences behind their backs, to such as haue power to redresse them. Quest. What is the second case wherein a man or woman may lawfully speake of the faults and offences of another or others, one or more, behind their backes? Answ. If it bee necessary that the partie or parties, one
or more to whom they speake, should be forewarned of those faults, in regard of danger either of some mischiefe, or some infection that may come to them from the same: as we may say to another or others one or more, take heede of such an one, I know he or she intends such a mischeife toward you: Act. 23.16. so when infection is feared from the partie or parties one or more; some one may say to another one or more, take heede you be not familiar with such a man or such a woman, for he or she is giuen to drunkennesse, to swearing, to whoredome or the like; and is not to bee accompanied withall. 1 Cor. 5.11. Quest. What are the speeches vttered of another or others one or more in publike, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others one or more? Answ. Speeches publikely vttered, either in the absence and behind the backe, or in the presence of the partie or par∣ties one or more, of whom they are spoken. Quest. What are the speeches publikely vttered in the absence and behinde the backe of the partie or parties one or more, of whom they are spoken, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of the partie or parties, one or more? Answ. Speeches either falsely charging some ill on another or others one or more, behinde their backs, and that either a∣gainst knowledge or on some light suspition: or truly char∣ging some ill on them behind their backs, out of malice, or for some by respect by way of publike information, without any calling thereunto: as when a man or woman doe either falsely, and that against knowledge, or on some light suspiti∣on, or truly out of their meere malice,Amos. 7.10. Act 25.2. or with respect to their owne profit only, informe some open Court, or some Magi∣strate and publike person, of some ill spoken or done by an∣other or others one or more, behinde their backes, being not called nor required so to speake. Thus did the Chaldeans. Dan. 3 8. to 13. Dan 6.13. Quest. What are the things publikely vttered in the presence of the partie or parties one or more, of whom they are vttered, that
are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of the partie or parties one or more? Answ. They are speeches vttered in open place of Iustice and iudgement, falsely, charging some ill on another or o∣thers, one or more in their presence, either by the Iudge or Iudges, one or more: or by Aduocates and Pleaders, or Pa∣trons of causes: or by Iurors, or by accusers, or by witnesses, one or more. Quest. What are the speeches vttered in open place of Iustice and iudgement, falsely charging some ill on another or others, one or more, by the Iudge or Iudges, one or more? Exod. 23.7. Leuit. 19.15. Pro. 17.15. Luk. 23.24.Answ. Speeches vttered by the Iudge or Iudges one or more, in giuing false sentence and vniust iudgement, against another or others one or more, being before them to bee ex∣amined and tried touching some matter of crime: as when the Iudge or Iudges one or more, doe either contrary to their owne knowledge, or without due examination and proofe, for feare, fauour, malice or the like, pronounce one or more being before them to be examined and tryed, guilty of some crime, and doe giue sentence against them for the same. Quest. What if the partie that is before a Iudge to be exami∣ned and tryed touching some crime, doe confesse himselfe guilty of that crime: is that confession sufficient to leade the Iudge to giue sentence against him? Answ. A bare confession is not sufficient, but a confession made after due examination taken on pregnant presumpti∣ons is sufficient:Iob 29.16. Pro. 18.13. for a man or a woman may confesse against themselues an vntruth, being vrged thereto by feare or threatning, or by a desire on some griefe to be put out of the world, or being perswaded it is the best course to saue their liues and to obtaine libertie, they may on simplicitie bee induced to confesse that which they neuer did, against themselues. Quest. What if the partie that is before a Iudge to bee exami∣ned and tryed touching some crime, be conuinced of that crime by witnesses: is that alwayes sufficient to leade the Judge to giue sen∣tence against him?
Answ. No, it is not; witnesses may be false,Deut. 19.18.19 and such as are not to be admitted, & the Iudge is to fift them throughly and to punish them if he finde them to be false. Quest. What are the speeches vttered in open place of Iustice and iudgement, by Aduocates, Pleaders, and Patrons of causes, falsely charging some ill on another or others one or more, in their presence? Answ. Speeches vttered by Aduocates, Pleaders and Pa∣trons of causes, in their false and vniust pleading against one or more, being in some open Court to bee examined and tried touching some matter of crime: as when Aduo∣cates, Pleaders, and Patrons of causes doe either contrary to their owne knowledge, or on light information, for feare, fauour, malice, or for their fee, vtter they care not what vn∣truths, and false calumniations in their pleading against one or more being in some open Court to bee examined and tryed touching some matter of crime:Pro. 25.18. Act. 24.2.5.6. hence then are their speeches compared to sharpe arrowes, wounding the good name of the innocent. Quest. What are the speeches vttered in open place of Justice and iudgement, by Iurors, falsely charging some ill on another or others one or more in their presence? Answ. Speeches vttered by Iurors in giuing vp a false and vniust verdict against one or more, being in some open Court to bee examined and tryed, touching some matter of crime: as when such as are on a Iury, doe either contrary to their owne knowledge, or on slight euidence without due proofe, for feare, fauour, malice, or the like: in their ver∣dict pronounce, one or more being examined in an open Court touching some matter of crime, guilty of that crime. Pro. 14.25.Pro. 14.25. so Iuors. Pro. 17.15.Pro. 17.15. not only Iudges but Iu∣rors also. Question. Who of a Jury are most faulty in giuing vp a false and vniust verdict against one or more being in some open Court to bee examined and tryed, touching some matter of crime? A. He or they, who either out of their malice, or for a bribe or such like, haue labored with the rest of the Iury, and haue
drawne them to ioyne with them in the same periury and corruption in giuing it vp.sai. 5.23. Quest. What are the speeches vttered in open place of Iustice and Iudgement, by accusers falsely charging some ill on another or others, one or more in their presence? euit. 19.16.Answ. Speeches vttered by accusers, whereby they doe vniustly and wrongfully accuse one or more, being in some open Court to bee examined and tryed, touching some mat∣ter of crime. Quest. How many waies doe men or women vniustly and wrongfully accuse one or more being in some open Court to bee ex∣amined, touching some matter of crime? Answer. Two wayes especially, Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; by doing it themselues, when men or wo∣men doe in their owne persons,Mat. 15.3. Act. 16.20. Act. 17.6.7. Act. 18.13. &. 25.7. wittingly, willingly, and maliciously, put vp an vniust and wrongfull accusation a∣gainst one or more, being in some open Court to bee exami∣ned, touching some matter of crime. Quest. What is the second way by which men or women doe vniustly and wrongfully accuse one or more, being in some open Court to be examined, touching some matter of crime? 1 King. 21.10: 11. &c. Mat. 26.59.60. Act. 6.11.Answ. This; by doing it by others, when a man or a wo∣man doe maliciously sub-orne another or others one or more, vniustly and wrongfully to accuse one or more being in some open Court to bee examined and tried, touching some matter of crime. Quest. What are the speeches vttered in open place of Iustice and iudgement, by witnesses falsely charging some ill on another or others one or more in their presence? Exod. 23.1. Pro. 6.19. &. 19.5.Answ. Speeches vttered by witnesses, whereby they doe vniustly testifie against one or more, being in some open Court to be examined and tryed, touching some matter of crime. Quest. How many waies doe witnesses vniustly testifie against one or more, being in some open Court to be examined and tryed, touching some matter of crime? Answ. Three wayes especially.
Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; by affirming something against them as witnesse, which they know is directly and materially false;1 King. 21.13 Acts 6.11.13. Acts 24.9. as when a man or woman doe wittingly and willingly for feare, fauour, malice, or for a reward, being suborned so to doe: affirme as witnesses that which they know is directly false, against one or more, being in some open Court to be ex∣amined and tryed touching some matter of crime. Quest. What is the second way by which witnesses doe vniustly testifie against one or more, being in some open Court to be exami∣ned and tryed, touching some matter of crime? Answ. This; by denying and concealing of something knowne to themselues to bee true, and which they ought to speake: as when a man or woman doe wittingly and willing∣ly for feare, fauour, malice, or for a reward; denie or con∣ceale, that which they know is true and ought to be witnes∣sed by them, being called so to doe: whereby one or more being in some open Court to be examined and tried, touch∣ing some matter of crime, come to be vniustly conuicted and condemned. Thus did the Iewes. Act. 24 21.Acts 24.21. Let those them∣selues say if they haue found any vniust thing in me, as if hee had said, these, if they would, can witnesse that they found no vn∣iust thing in me, while I stood in the Councell: but they conceale the truth. Quest: What is the third way by which witnesses doe vniustly testifie against one or more, being in some open Court to bee exami∣ned and tried, touching some matter of crime? Answ. This; by affirming something against them, as wit∣nesses, craftily and deceitefully; as when a man or woman doe wittingly and willingly for feare, fauour, malice, or for a bribe, being suborned so to witnesse something against one or more, being in some open Court to be examined and try∣ed touching some matter of crime: either by taking from the truth, or by adding to it, or by changing of it; as by wrest∣ing their sayings to another sense then they were spokē. Thus dealt the witnesses against our Sauiour Christ, Mat. 26.61. compared with John. 2.19,
Quest. How may the vglinesse of the sinne of false witnesse bearing in open place of Iustice and iudgement appeare? Answ. By this; because it is there deliuered vpon oath, so that a false witnesse in open place of iudgement, is guilty not only of false witnesse bearing, but of periurie also; where∣by he polluteth the holy name of God, wrongeth the inno∣cent, abuseth the Iudge and Iury, and all that are present, and that vnder religion of an oath. Quest. Whether is false witnesse bearing in open place of Justice and iudgement, or slandering in priuate, more grieuous? Answ. In respect of the oath taken, and of the greater in∣famie following on it; false witnesse bearing in open place of Iustice and iudgement, is more grieuous then priuate slan∣dering: the thing spoken of being the same, and the circum∣stances of it being alike. But the priuate slanderer may haue a more malicious intent, then he which falsely deposeth in o∣pen place of Iustice and iudgement: and if his false report in priuate touch his Neighbours life, he is more iniurious then he which publikely witnesseth falsely, where the crime bringeth not the life in question. Question. What are the things on the part of the hearer or hearers one or more, vttered of another or others one or more, that are contrary to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of another or others one or more? Answer. Speeches heard and willingly receiued and en∣tertained by the hearer or hearers one or more, being con∣trary to the truth, and tending to the hurt or hinderance of the good name of the partie or parties one or more of whom they are spoken:Exod. 23.1. Psal. 15.3. Prou. 17.4. as when a man or woman doe giue eare to, and willingly receiue and entertaine such speeches as are vttered of another or others one or more, contrarie to the truth, and tend to the hurt or hinderance of their good names. Quest. How many waies doe men or women giue eare to, and willingly receiue and entertaine such speeches as are vttered of an∣other or others one or more, contrary to the truth, and tending to the hurt and hinderance of their good names?
Answ. Two wayes especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; by beleeuing, and easily giuing credit to flying tales & ill reports, that are made of another or o∣thers one or more, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true, and thereupon iudge amisse of them, or hating them, or contemning them:Gen. 39.19. 1 Sam. 24.10. 2 Sam. 16.4. Prou. 14.15. Ier. 37.15. Acts 14.28. as when a man or woman are too credulous, and do too easily beleeue the report of ill that is made of another or others one or more, and doe presently on the report, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true, and without sufficient euidence and ground, thinke ill of them, or hate them, or contemne them. Quest. Who are most faulty in beleeuing, and easily giuing credit to flying tales and ill reports that are made of another or o∣thers one or more, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true? Answ. They who beleeue them and giue credit to them so farre, as they blaze or spread them further abroad,Exod. 23.1.  Psal 15.3.  and it may bee adde to them, and thinke they are excusable in so doing; because they are not the first Authours of them. Exod. 23.1. The word  of the roote  signifies thou shalt not take vp, and so it importeth both the first ray∣sing, and the after receiuing, and reporting of a flying tale: so Psal. 15.3. Quest. What is the second way by which men or women doe giue eare to, and willingly receiue and entertaine, such speeches as are vttered of another or others one or more, contrary to the truth, and tending to the hurt or hinderance of their good name? Answ. This; by hearing of ill reports that are made of an∣other or others one or more, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true, yet suspecting them to be false; with pa∣tience and silence, and shewing no dislike to them at all, ei∣ther by countenance or speech, or turning away, or the like: as when a man or woman do heare ill reports that are made of another or others one or more, they not knowing the thing or things reported to be true,Prou. 25.23. Ephes. 5.11. in silēce & with a smiling counte∣nance, & such behauiour as they seeme to approue of them as
commending the reporter or reporters one or more, bidding them to their Table, or some way or other countenancing or rewarding them. Quest. Who are most faulty in hearing ill reports that are made of another or others one or more, with patience and silence, and in shewing no dislike of them at all? Answ. They who on their owne knowledge can testifie that the thing or things reported be false and iniurious, and yet either for flatterie, or for feare of displeasing, are silent and doe not open their mouthes to cleere the innocent, and to shew the truth of the matter: this is to sinne against the Law of Nature, which teacheth vs to doe as we would be done by, Mat. 7.12. and we would that others hearing vs tradu∣ced, and knowing vs innocent should speake in our defence: and therefore we must doe the like. Quest. How may the vglinesse of the sinne of hearing and wil∣ling receiuing and entertaining of speeches vttered of another or o∣thers one or more, contrary to the truth, and tending to the hurt or hinderance of their good names, appeare? Answ. By this; because it argues a delight in hearing the faults and offences of others, which is a note of a wicked person;Pro. 17.4. Reuel. 22.15. and in so doing, men or women take pleasure in hearing those things whereby God is dishonoured, the salua∣tion of others hindered, their good name impayred, and the iudgements of God prouoked. Quest. When is hearing and willing receiuing and entertai∣ning of speeches vttered of another or others, one or more, contrary to the truth, and tending to the hurt or hinderance of their good names: whether it be light beleeuing of ill reports, or hearing them with patience and silence, and shewing no dislike of them at all, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true, most vile and most odious? Answ. When men or women doe heare, and willingly re∣ceiue and entertaine,Psal. 38.16. Ierem. 20.10. 1 Tim. 5.19. and doe either easily beleeue, or heare with patience and silence, and without shewing any dislike at all, ill reports that are made of such as are truly religious and truly feare God, not knowing the thing or things repor∣ted to be true: as if some impudent person, shall come and
buze in their eares some odions tale against true professours of the Gospell; they presently imbrace it, and it goes for currant with them, as if nothing were more sure: this is most vile and odious. Quest. When is hearing and willing receiuing, and entertai∣ning of speeches vttered of another or others, one or more, contrary to the truth, and tending to the hurt or hinderance of their good names: whether it be by light beleeuing of ill reports, or hearing of them with patience and silence, and shewing no dislike of them, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true: most pernici∣ous and most hurtfull? Answ. When Magistrates, such as bee in authority, doe heare and willingly receiue, and entertaine,Gen. 39.20. 1 Sam. 22.17.18.19. Hst. 3.13.14. and doe easily beleeue or heare with patience & silence, and without shew∣ing any dislike at all, ill reports that are made of another or others, one or more, not knowing the thing or things repor∣ted, to be true. Quest. Whether is the tale bearer, or the tale hearer and recei∣uer, a more grieuous sinner? Answ. The tale hearer and receiuer; because the tale hearer and receiuer, is not only guilty of the same offence with the tale bearer; but he encourageth him in his sinne, & he giues being to the slander: a theefe may rob his Neighbour of his goods without a receiuer, but a tale bearer cannot rob a man of his good name, nor yet impayre his credit, vnlesse there be another or others, one or more, to heare and to admit his slanders: he may shew his malice, but the partie of whom he speakes he cannot hurt, vnlesse there be one or more to heare him. Quest. May not a man or woman heare, and willingly receiue and entertaine the report of ill, touching another or others, one or more, at all? Answ. Yes, they may in two cases lawfully. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This;Gen. 37.2. 1 Cor. 1.11. if they haue power and authority ouer the partie or parties one or more, whose faults are reported, and may examine them, and finding them faulty, may admonish or punish them for the same. Quest. What is the second case wherein a man or woman may
lawfully heare, and willingly receiue and entertaine the report of ill, touching another or others, one or more? Answ. This; if it be expedient that they should bee fore∣warned of the ill that is reported, in regard of the danger to them, either of iniurie or of infection. Thus Paul might heare the report of his sisters sonne. Acts. 25.16. so one may heare and willingly receiue an ill report, for the auoyding of their company, they being not to be accompanied withall. Now to the Affirmatiue part. Quest. What doth the ninth Commandement require? Answ. In generall; whatsoeuer is agreeable to the truth, and tends to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of a man or woman. Quest. What are the things that are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe nnd furtherance of the good name of a man or woman? Answ. Either such things as are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe and furtherance of a man or a womans owne good name; or such things as are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of an∣other or others, one or more. Quest. What are the things that are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe and furtherance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. They are either things inward in the heart, or things expressed and vttered by the tongue. Quest. What are the things inward in the heart, that are a∣greeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe and furtherance of a man, or a womans owne good name? Answ. Two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Sam. 18.18. Prou. 3.7. Isai. 5.21. Rom. 12.16. 2 Cor. 10.12.13.14. 2 Cor. 13.5.Answ. This; a right iudgement and estimation of them∣selues, & of their owne good gifts; neither ouer-weening, nor vnderweening of them. A man or woman are to know them∣selues to be that which indeede they are: & truly & rightly to iudge of themselues, and of the good things that be in them and of the measure of them: they are to know, and to iudge truly of their owne wants and infirmities.
Quest. What is the second thing inward in the heart, that is agreeable to the truth, & tends to the helpe or furtherance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. This; a loue of their owne good name, and a care of their credit, expressing that by all good endeauour,Prou. 22.1. 2 Cor. 8.20.21. Phil. 4.8. to get a good name, and being gotten, to keepe it: and if at any time it be through sin impayred or lost, to recouer it. A man or woman must loue their owne good name, and haue a care of their credit: & they are to endeauour by all good meanes, to get a good name; and hauing gotten it, to continue it: and it being at any time, by some sinne impayred or lost, to re∣couer it. Quest. How is a man or woman to endeauour to get a good name, and hauing gotten it, to keepe it?Prou. 10.7. Luke 1.6. Iohn 1.47. Acts 16.2. Rom. 14.18. Heb. 11.2. Eccles. 10.1. 1 Sam. 2.30. Answ. By liuing religiously, embracing the truth of God in loue to it, and practising it in an holy life, sincerely and without dissimulation, keeping a narrow watch against e∣uery sin, and with an honest and vpright heart, seeking Gods glory in euery thing. Quest. How is a man or woman to recouer a good name, it be∣ing either impayred or lost through sin? Answ. By true repentance, and vnfeigned conuersation,2 Cor. 2.7.8. Coloss. 4.9. Philem. epist. vers. 10. and turning to God, and breaking of that sin, and by testify∣ing the same before men, by amandment of life. Quest. Is a man or a woman bound to seeke the approbation of men, & are they to approue themselues & their actions, to men? Answ. Though they may not be men pleasers,Galat. 1.10. Rom. 15.2. 1 Cor. 10.33. Rom. 12.17. 2 Cor. 8.21. by framing and tempering their speeches and their actions according to the corrupt humours, and wicked affections and dispositions of men, yet may they please them in that which is good to e∣dification: and they may and ought to seeke the approbati∣on of men, some cautions being duly obserued. Quest. What are the cautions that are to be obserued in seeking the approbation of men? Answ. Foure especially. Quest. What is the first of those? A. This; that it be a seeking of Gods approbation also, and with a seeking of that in the first place: a man or woman may
and ought to seeke the approbation of men, in their speeches and actions, 5.44.  12.43.  2.52. . 14.12. r. 10.18. so as they rest not in that alone, but withall doe seeke to be approued of God, & do seeke for his approbation in the first place: & then in the second place to be approued of men. Quest. What is the second caution that is to be obserued in seeking the aepprobation of men? 6.26.  5.41.Answ. This; that it be without ambition and vaine glory, and without seeking popular applause: a man or woman, may and ought to seeke the approbation of men, so as they be not addicted to popular applause, and do not immoderately seeke the approbation of the multitude, and to get themselues fame with all sorts of men, both good and bad. Quest. What is the third caution that is to be obserued in see∣king the approbation of men? Ans. This; that it be without giuing the least iust occasion of offence to any; a man or woman may, and ought to seeke the approbation of men,r. 10.32. t. 2.12. yea of wicked men, so farre as they giue not the least iust occasion of offence to them. Quest. What is the fourth caution that is to bee obserued in seeking the approbation of men? A. This; that it be with a carefull & conscionable doing of their duties in their particular honest & lawful places & cal∣ling.or. 4.3. or. 6.8. A man or woman may and ought to seeke the approba∣tion of men; so as it be in a carefull and conscionable doing of their duties in their particular, honest, and lawfull places & calling: fearing neither the faces nor the censures of men. Quest. What are the things that are expressed and vttered by the tongue, that are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe & furtherance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. Three especially. Quest. What is the first of those? rou. 10.19. rou. 13.2. ath. 12.36. Tim. 4.7.  Tim. 2.16.Answ. This; speaking sparingly, and avoyding vaine bab∣bling. A man or a woman must bee sparing in speaches, in their ordinarie communication: and they are to auoyd fraud, and foolish talke, and idle and fruitlesse speeches. Quest. May not a man or woman speake of worldly matters? Answ. Yes, they may; so as it bee in due time and place, and so as their speeches therein sauour of grace,Prou. 15.23.  Coloss. 4.6. and bee for the good one of another.
Quest. What is the second thing expressed and vttered by the tongue, that is agreeable to the truth & tends to the helpe & fur∣therance of a man or a womans owne good name? Answ. This; a wise and discreete speaking, when they haue occasion either to mention their vertues & good things, or their faults and euill things to men. Quest. Wherein stands a man or a womans wise & discreet spea∣king, hauing occasion to mention their vertues and good things to men? Answ. In speaking of them with modestie:Pro. 27.2. Ioh. 8.13. 1 Cor. 15.9. a man or a wo∣man hauing occasion to mention the good things that are in themselues, or the good things done by them, tending to their commendation, to men, they are to speake of them with mo∣destie, and so as their speech incline rather to the defect then to the excesse; and so as they rather extenuate them then boast of them, and giue men occasion to iudge them arrogant or vaine-glorious. Quest. Wherein stands a man or womans wise and discreete speaking, hauing occasion to mention their faults and euill things to men? Answ. In speaking of their knowne faults and corrupti∣ons to men, the vttermost they can against themselues;Galat. 1.13. 1 Tim. 1.13.15 yet so as they giue no suspition of pride or hypocrisie, and so as they doe not disgrace themselues so much as they make themselues able to doe lesse good then otherwise they might. And in speaking of their secret faults and corruptions to men only when it is fit and meete for them so to doe. Quest. When is it fit and meete for a man or woman to speake of their secret faults and corruptions to men? Answ. In two cases only. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; in case of secret offence and wrong done to another or others one or more. A man or woman hauing se∣cretly offended and wronged another or others one or more: it is fit and meete they should freely & of their owne accord, and plainely acknowledge that offence & wrong to them, and craue pardon of them for it; if they can come to them: so as the partie or parties wronged be such as will not take aduan∣tage
on their acknowledgement, and vse extreamity against them for the same, and so that place Mat. 5.23. is to bee vn∣derstood. Qu. What is the second case wherein it is fit & meete for a man or woman to speake of their secrot faults and corruptions to men? Answ. This; in case of trouble of minde and conscience. A man or woman being troubled in minde and conscience for some secret fault & corruption, it is fit and meet they should freely & of their owne accord, 5.16. . 4.8. lay open the thing that trou∣bles their conscience, and speake of it to another or others one or more, so as it be to such as can and will, being pitty∣full, minister a word of comfort and counsell to them: and to such as are faithfull, and will keepe things secret that are reuealed to them. Quest. What is the third thing expressed and vttered by the tongue, that is agreeable to the truth and tends to the helpe or fur∣therance of a man or womans owne good name? Answ. This; a speaking in defence of their owne good name when neede requireth.am. 1.15. or. 12.11.12 A man or woman must (as they are able) speake in the defence of their owne good name, and of their owne innocency when neede requireth, so as they doe it modestly and vnwillingly. Quest. What are the things that are agreeable to the truth, & tend to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or o∣thers one or more? Answ. Either things inward in the heart, or things ex∣pressed and vttered by the tongue. Quest. What are the things inward in the heart that are a∣greeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. They are three things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? en. 37.33. Mat. 7.1. Mat. 26.10.11 Mar. 10.13.14 Rom. 1.29. 1 Cor. 13.5.Answ. This; a charitable opinion and estimation of an∣other or others one or more, and a thinking the best of things said or done by them, & a taking of them in good part so farre as truth & reason will giue leaue. A man or a woman are to thinke and to iudge charitably both of the persons of others, and of their words and deeds, so far as they may with
truth and reason, and where there is no euident cause to the contrary: and they are to interpret things that are said or done by them being euill, yet doubtfull and vncertaine, and such as will beare two constructions in the best part, and in the most fauourable manner that may be. Quest. What is the second thing inward in the heart, that is agreeable to the truth, and tends to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Ans. This; a true loue and an hearty welwishing to the good name of another or others, one or more:Mat. 1.19. a man or wo∣man must carry in their hearts a true loue and good affection to the credit of another or others, one or more: and they are heartily to wish well to their good name. Quest. How may a man or woman know that they truly loue, and heartily wish well to the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. By two things. Quest. What is the first of those?Rom. 1.8. 1 Cor. 12.26. Galat. 5.22. Answ. This; by reioycing for their credit and good esti∣mation, they knowing them on good grounds, to be in good credit, and in good estimation. Quest: What is the second thing whereby a man or woman may know that they truly loue and heartily wish well to the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. This;Ezech. 9.3.4. 1 Cor. 12.20. by greeuing when they know they deserue discredit and disgrace, when they heare a true report of the same ill spoken or done by them, whereby they are iustly blemished, an their reputation is iustly diminished. Quest. What is the third thing inward in the heart that is a∣greeable to the truth, and tends to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. This; a staiednesse of iudgement touching ill reports that are made of another or others one or more. A man or woman hearing an ill report made of another or others one or more, not knowing the thing or things reported to be true; they are to suspend their iudgement touching the person or the persons, and touching the thing or things reported, and not presently and easily to beleeue them, but to make further
search into them, as they may, not going beyond the bounds of their calling. Psal. 15.3. Pro. 17.4. This the Lord teacheth by his owne example. Gen. 11.5. Gen. 18.21. Quest. What are the things expressed and vttered by the tongue that are agreeable to the truth, and ten to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. They are things vttered either to another or others, one or more, or of another or others one or more. Quest. What are the things vttered to another or others, one or more, that are agreeable to the truth, & tend to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answer. Two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? 5.2. . 8.16. . 4.25.Answ. This; a speaking of the truth from the heart, sim∣ply and plainely as it ought to be spoken. A man or a woman must speake the simple truth to another or others one or more, without ambiguity or doubtfulnesse, or doubling: and as neere as they can, so as their words may bee cleare to the vnderstanding of the hearer or hearers, one or more. Quest. How ought the simple and plaine truth to be spoken? m. 22.9.10 . 8 19. m. 17.18.16.17.Answ. With good affection and with a louing heart, with an intent & a desire to doe good by speaking of it, & seaso∣nably, a man or woman hauing a calling to speake it. Quest. What is the second thing vttered by the tongue to an∣other or others, one or more, that is agreeable to the truth, and tends to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. This; a wise and discreete speaking to another or others, one or more, for their good, as iust occasion is offered. Quest. Wherein stands a wise and discreete speaking to another or others one or more, for their good, as occasion is offered? Answ. In two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? . 15.4. o. 19.20. ct. 18.26. oloss. 3.16. Thess. 5.11.Answ. This; in giuing them wholesome aduice & counsel in matters of doubt, & in directing them in the waies of God, and exhorting and stirring them vp to walke threin in loue and wisedome. A man or woman must, as they are able and as occasion is offered, keeping themselues within
the bounds of their callings, wisely and in loue both giue wholesome counsell to others in matters of doubt, and also direct them in the wayes of God, and exhort and stirre them vp to walke therein. Quest. What is the second thing wherein standeth a wise and discreet speaking to another or others, one or more, for their good, as occasion is offered? Answ. This;Leuit. 19.17. Mat. 18.15. Luk. 17.3. Coloss. 13.6. 1 Thess. 5.14. Tit. 1.13. in giuing them sound and seasonable admoni∣tion and iust reproofe for their knowne faults and sinnes in loue and wisdome. A man or a woman must, as they are able, and as occasion is offered, keeping themselues within the bounds of their callings, wisely and in loue admonish and reprooue others for their knowne faults and offences. Rom. 16.17. The authors of heresies, schismes, and dissentions are to be auoyded, and we are to haue nothing to do with them; therefore they are not to be reproued. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; that place must be vnderstood with a par∣ticular limitation, that they must be auoided after once or twice admonition, Tim. 3.10. Quest. How doth a man or woman wisely, louingly, and seaso∣nably reprooue another or others, one or more, for their knowne faults and offences? Answ. By doing it with due obseruation of some rules that are necessarily to be obserued in the doing of it. Quest. What are those necessary rules that are to bee obserued in reprouing of others for their knowne faults and offences? Answ. Three especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. This; that the reproofe bee fitted,1 Kin. 5 13. 1 Tim. 5.1.2. Luk. 23.40. Tit. 1.13. Galat. 6.1. 2 Thess. 3.15. as neere as may be, to the qualitie and condition of the party reproued, and to the nature of the offence for which the partie offnding is iustly reprooued. A man or a woman must as neere as they can, fit their reproofe of the knowne faults of others, to the qualitie and condition of the persons whom they doe re∣proue; friendly reproouing their equalls reuerently and sub∣missiuely exhorting their Superiours, and sharply and yet in loue and compassion reprouing their inferiours: and they
must also as neere as they can,d: epist. vs 2.23. fit their reproofe of the known faults to the nature of the offence, reproouing sinnes com∣mitted of ignorance or humane frailtie with mildnesse and gentlenesse; and sinnes done of malice, of pride and presump∣tion, with sharpnesse and seueritie. Quest. What is the second necessary rule that is to be duely ob∣serued in reprouing of others for their knowne faults? Answ. This; that the reproofe be vsed in the fittest time and season,Sam. 25.6.37. ro. 25.11. when it may doe most good, both to bring the partie reprooued to a sight of his sinne, and to reclaime him or her, bee it man or woman from that sinne. A man or wo∣man must (as neere as they can) take the fittest time to re∣prooue the knowne faults of others, and then reprooue them when they may doe them most good by their reproofe; as they are not to tell a man of his fault being drunke, or in the heate of his passion, but afterward when he comes to himselfe. Quest. What is the third necessary rule that is to bee duely ob∣serued in reprouing of others for their knowne faults? Answ.
