This; that the reproofe of others for their sinnes knowne onely to our selues or to others but a few, be vsed as secretly as may be, and without open disgrace to the party or parties reprooued.Mat. 18.15. Luk. 17 3.  Pet. 4.8. A man or woman must bee as secret as they may, in reproouing others for their sinnes knowne one∣ly to themselues or to others, but a few, and must be carefull of their credit in reprouing them, and not disgracing them openly before many: for open disgracefull rebuking of men will rather harden them in their sinnes, then reclaime them from sinne. Prou. 27.5. Open rebuke is better then secret loue: It seemes therefore that men for their knowne sinnes are to bee rebu∣ked openly. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; by Open rebuke in that place, is not meant rebuke in the presence of many, or openly, but pri∣uate rebuke giuen to the face of the offender, and not be∣hinde his backe, which may be betweene the reproouer, and the reprooued alone.
1 Tim. 5.20. Them that sinne, rebuke openly, that others may feare: Therefore men are for their knowne sinnes to be reprooued openly. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; those words, Them that sinne, rebuke openly, are not a generall commandement giuen to all, but a speciall commandement giuen to Pastours or Gouernours of the Church, that they should reprooue those Elders, and conse∣quently all such as were conuinced of any crime by witnes∣ses, & that before all men; that is, before the whole Church, & and not before all men in euery place and assembly where they offend, and that appeares, ver. 19. Quest. Is a man or a woman euer bound to the dutie of re∣proofe; and are they at all times bound to reprooue others for their knowne faults and offences? Answ. No; in some cases they are not bound, there be some particular cases wherein a man or a woman is not bound to reproue others for their knowne faults and offences. Quest. What are those particular cases? Answ. Three especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. If the party or parties one or more, offending,2 Cor. 2.6.7. haue truly repented of their faults and offences, and haue giuen apparant signes of their vnfained repentance, they are not then to be reproued for those faults and offencs: for the end of reproofe is to reclaime the offender; and if hee be already reclaimed, there is no place left for reproofe. Quest. VVhat is the second particular case wherein a man or woman is not bound to reprooue others for their knowne faults and offences? Ans. This; if it be certaine and euident,Pro. 9.7.8. Pro. 23.9. Mat. 7.6. that the reproofe will do no good: for where there is no hope of amendment, (which is the end of reproofe) the reproofe is to be omitted, especiay if it be so farre from bettering the partie repro∣ued, that it makes him or her much worse. The Magistrate ceaseth not to punish male factors, though it be so, that they haue either truely repented of their faults or offences, or that they are not bettered by punishment:
to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. Either things vttered by such as sit as Iudges in some open place of Iustice and Iudgment; or things vttered by others that are lawfully called to speake before them, ei∣ther as Aduocates and Patrons of causes, or as Iurours, or as witnesses. Quest. What are the things that are vttered of another or o∣thers. one or more in publike, by such as sit as Iudges in some open place of Iustice and Iudgement, that are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or o∣thers, one or more? Answ. Two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. This; the absoluing and acquitting of such as come before them, and after due examination and triall touching some matter of crime laid against them,ro. 18.5. ro. 31.9. ere. 26.16. Luk. 23.14. o. 22. are found guiltles; & the pronouncing of them innocent, and free from the crimes falsely obiected against them: such as sit as Iudges in open place of Iudgement, are to absolue and acquite such persons as before them haue bin duly examined and tried, touching some matter of crime, and found guiltlesse; and they are o∣penly to pronounce them innocent, and free from the crimes falsely obiected against them. Quest. What is the second thing vttered of another or others, one or more in publike, by such as sit as Iudges in some open place of iudgement, that is agreeable to the truth, and tends to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Iob. 29.25. Rom. 13.3.Answ. This; a due encouragement of such as are before them, and on some iust occasion are made knowne to them to bee honest and good, and to deserue well, and a giuing of them due praise and commendation for their well doing. Such as sit as Iudges in open places of Iudgement, are to encourage such persons as come before them, being made knowne to them on iust occasion to be honest and good; and they are to praise and commend them, wherein they doe any way iustly deserue well. Quest. What are the things vttered of another or others, one
or more in publike, by such as are lawfully called to speake in some open place of Judgement, either as Aduocates, or as Iurours, or as witnesses that are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe and furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. Speeches vttered by them in the defence of the good name of another or others, one or more, and for the clearing of their innocencie, when they are to their know∣ledge openly wronged, and falsely accused of some crime:Pro. 12.6. Pro. 14.25. Pro. 24.11. Aduocates, Iurours, and Witnesses, that are lawfully called to speake in some open place of Iudgment, must there speake in the defence of the good name of others; and for the clea∣ring of them whom they know to be falsely accused of some crime. Quest. When are Aduocates, Iurors, and Witnesses that are lawfully called to speake in some open place of Iudgement, especi∣ally bound to performe this dutie? Answ. When the parties openly wronged,Iob. 29.12. Pro. 31.8. and falsely ac∣cused, are helplesse, and either cannot, or dare not speake for themselues. Quest. What are the things on the part of the hearer or hearers, one or more, touching things vttered by the tongue of another or o∣thers, one or more, that are agreeable to the truth, and tend to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or others, one or more? Answ. Two things especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. A ready receiuing of the good report that is made of another or others, one or more,Hest. 9.4. Act. 16.2.3. 1 Cor. 13.7. so farre as truth and rea∣son will giue leaue. A man or a woman must willingly and readily receiue the report of good that is made of others, one or more, so farre as they may with truth and reason, and they not knowing any thing to the contrary. Quest. Who are most and principally bound to this dutie, rea∣dily to receiue the report of good that is made of others, one or more, so farre as they may with truth and reason, and they not knowing any thing to the contrary? Ans. They who are bound to the particular parties, one or more, of whom the report is made, by some neere bond, either of nature or religion, or place & habitation, neighborhood, or
the like; for a man is especially to loue and regard those that are more neerely knit to him: hence the Apostle saith, 1 Tim. 5.8. If there be any that prouideth not for his owne, and namely for them of his houshold, he denieth the faith, and is worse then an In∣fidell. And Salomon saith, He that raiseth vp contentions among brethren, Prou. 6.19. is most odious. iectionProu. 14.15. The foolish man will beleeue euery thing. It is a fault, and the part of a foole to beleeue euery thing that is brought to him: Therefore it seemes that a man or woman must not readily receiue the report of any good that is made of others, one or more. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; the meaning of that place is, that one who is silly for his owne soule, and ignorant in the matters of God, and of Religion, is ready to yeeld to any thing that is sayd to him, to draw him into errour or sinne, and hee rashly giues credit to euery vaine tale that is told him, and hee hearkeneth to euery spirit, and to euery deceiuer, that misse-leads him contrary to that, 1 Iohn 4.1.Iohn 4.1. and so it makes not against this, that wee must readily receiue the re∣port of any good that is made of others, one or more, so farre as we may with truth and reason, and not knowing any thing to the contrary. Quest. VVhat is the second thing on the part of the hearer or hearers, one or more, touching things vttered by the tongue of another or others, one or more, that is agreeable to the truth, and tends to the helpe or furtherance of the good name of another or o∣thers, one or more? Answ. This; a shewing dislike of whisperers and tale-bearers,Exod. 23.1. Psal. 15.3. Prou. 25.23. when a man or woman doe heare ill reported of an∣other or others, one or more, by such as they haue iust cause to suspect, and to think to be whisperers or tale-bearers, they are to shew their dislike of them, either by countenance, or speech, or by gesture, or the like. Quest. Who are most and principally bound to this duetie, to shew dislike of whisperers and tale-bearers? Psal. 101.5.Ans. Magistrates, by such as be in any place of authoritie and superioritie.
The tenth Commandement. Thou shalt not couet thy neighbours house, neither shalt thou couet thy neighbours Wife, nor his Manseruant, nor his Maid, nor his Oxe, nor his Asse, neither any thing that is thy neighbours. Quest. What difference is there betweene the tenth Comman∣dement, and the other Commandements foregoing? Answ. This; in the former Commandements is forbidden both the euill act, and also the euill thought setled, & with full & deliberate consent of wil; but in the tenth commandement is forbidden the euill thought, and euery motion and stirring in the soule that is contrary to charititie and loue of others, though no liking or consent of will be giuen to it. Quest. What are the words of the tenth Commandement? Answ. Those we find, Exo. 20.17. Thou shalt not couet thy neighbours house, neither shalt thou couet thy neighbours wife, nor his manseruant, nor his mayd, nor his oxe, nor his asse, neither any thing that is thy neighbours. Quest. VVhy is this Commandement set downe in so many words, and so many particulars? Ans. Because in this commandment the Lord laies a more strict rule, and a straighter charge on the soule of man, then flesh and blood would willingly beare: for men would haue their secret euill thoughts, & their least euill affections free, and not subiect to any law; and they thinke it too rigorous, and too hard to haue them called into question, & to be con∣demned therefore; the Lord is, as it were, constrained to set downe this commandement by particular branches, that men might find no evasion, nor any way to wind themselues from vnder the compasse of this commandement. Quest. Are these words, Thou shalt not couet thy neighbors house, thou shalt not couet thy neighbors wife, nor his man-seruant, nor his mayd, nor his oxe, nor his asse, neither any thing that is thy neigbours, onely one Commandement, or two as the Papists teach? Answ. Onely one commandement and not two; for that which is here put downe in the first place (thou shalt not couet thy neighbors house) is put in the second place; and that which
is here put in the second place touching the neighbors wife, is put in the first place: which Moses would not haue done, had they bin distinct precepts: he there making a repetition of the Commandements. 5.21. And again, the Apostle Paul speaks of concupiscence, of coueting, or of lust, as one precept, Rom. 7.7. therefore these words make but one Commandement. ction.Those things that are so diuers, that one may bee coueted and not the other, belong not to one precept, but one may co∣uet his Neighbours wife, and not couet any thihg of his be∣sides: and therefore these two kinds of couetings, of the wife and of the house, belong not to one Commandement. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; by this reason the two first Commandements of the first Table, are two distinct precepts which the Pa∣pists confound and make but one: for one may be guilty of Idolatrie & false worship, who yet holdeth but one God. Se∣condly, that proposition of coueting that which is not ioy∣ned with another thing, belongs not to the same precept, is false, for one may couet a mans house & ground, that couets not his Oxe,ing. 21.2.3 or Asse: as Ahab did, who coueted Naboths vine∣yard. And so by this rule, as many particulars as are heere set downe which may be seuerally coueted, so many particular precepts against coueting there should be. ection.The act of Adultery, and the act of Theft are diuers, and belong to two diuerse precepts: therefore diuers concupi∣scences tending to these diuers acts, are to be diuided into two precepts. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the argument is not good, because the acts of Adulterie & Theft are forbidden in two diuers precepts, therefore concupiscences tending thereunto should be so: for there is difference betweene the conceptiō of sin, & the birth and perfection of it: when sin is brought forth and perfected, then it appeareth of what kinde it is; but being yet in the seed and conception, it cannot be so distinguished. 1 Iohn. 2.16. The lust of the flesh, and the lust of the eyes are distinguished, therefore they are distinctly forbidden, and be∣long not to one and the same Commandement.
Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; the lust of the flesh, and the lust of the eies, being two distinct lusts, are distinctly to be expressed: but it followes not therefore that they are to be distinguished into two precepts, and that they belong not to one and the same Commandement, and so it still remaines a truth, that the last precept which forbids all manner of coueting, is not to bee deuided into two precepts, but is one whole and intire com∣mandement, consisting of diuers particulars. Quest. What are the generall things contained in these words. Thou shalt not couer. &c. Answ. These two things. First a prohibition, a forbid∣ding of lust or coueting, Thou shalt not couet or lust after. And secondly, a reckoning vp of some particulars, that lust may be vnlawfully carried vnto, & which may be vnlawful∣ly coueted and lusted after: as the Neighbours house, the Neighbours wife, his man seruant, his maide, his Oxe, his Asse, or any other thing that is his. Quest. What is here meant when the Lord faith, Thou shalt not couet? Answ. The word couet,Ierem. 4.14. Mat. 15.19. Iam. 1.14. signifieth both inwardly to thinke on something in the minde, and also in the heart to incline to∣wards it with delight, and to long a feer it, yet without any consent of will or purpose of heart to seeke after it: and so the meaning of these words Thou shalt not couet, is this. Thou shalt not inwardly thinke on, and withall haue thine heart inclined to, with pleasure and delight, and long after that which belongs to another or others, one or more: to his or their losse or hinderance, or misliking, though they will giue no assent to get it or to seeke af∣ter it. The word Neighbour is here to be taken as in the ninth Commandement: for any one of the same flesh, and of the same nature, which is any man or woman whatsoeuer. Quest. What is heere meant by house, Thou shalt not cou thy Neighbours house? Answ. Not only the timber, and other materiall things whereof the house is made, and the frame of it, but also any o∣ther thing belonging to it: as furniture within it, grounds without it, yeelding any fruite or benefit, and euery
thing in or about the house, ground or field, moueable, or vn∣moueable, which is either for profit or for pleasure. Quest. What are we here to vnderstand by Wife? Ans. Not only the wife who is one flesh with her husband by matrimoniall bond, and his chiefest treasure, Gen. 39.9. but the husband also who is one flesh with his wife: for as man is restrained of his lust to his neighbours wife, so is woman to her neighbours husband; and the law reacheth not to one sex alone, but to both. Other things in this Commandement need not be stood vpon. By any thing that is his: the Lord comprehends in these words euery thing how small soeuer in our account, that belongs to our neighbour. Quest. What is the ground of this prohibition, thou shalt not in thy minde inwardly thinke on, and withall haue thine heart inclined to with pleasure and delight, and long after that which belongs to another or others, one or more, to his or their losse or mis-liking, though thy will giue no consent to get it, or to seeke after it? Answ. Both the maintenance of inward purity according that original purity in righteousnes & holines in which man was first perfectly created according to the image of God. 1.27. s. 4.24. And also the maintenance of true and perfect obedience to God, not onely in the purpose and resolution of his heart, and in his words and deeds, but also in his most secret thoughts, and in the in-most hidden motions of his soule,t. 27.26. and so stand in all the words of the Law to doe them. Quest. What is the summe of this Commandement? Answ. That in the least thought, and in-most inward dis∣position of the heart we decline not from the rule of charitie and loue of others, either the loue of God or men, but that in our most secret thoughts and motions of our soules,k. 10.27. we keepe our selues within the rule of true loue towards others, both towards God, and towards men. Loue thinkes not euill. 1. Cor. 13.5. The Negatiue part of this Commandement. Quest. VVhat doth the tenth Commandement forbid?
Answ. Two things in generall. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. The proness and inclinations of our corrupt na∣ture to euill, whereby a man or woman is naturally prone to thinke, will, or affect any thing that is forbidden in the Law of God, and contrary to the true loue of God or man. Rom. 6.12. The Apostle speakes of sinne and the lusts of it; and this is called the law of the members, Rom. 7.23. and the flesh, Galat. 5.24. distinct from the lusts of it. Quest. Is pronesse and inclination to euill in euery man and woman naturally?Psal. 51.5. Ephes. 2.3. Answ. Yes, it is in euery man and woman descending from Adam by naturall generation: euery man and woman comming from Adam by naturall generation, is conceiued and borne in sinne, and so hath an inbred pronesse, and in∣clination to euill, and to that which the Law of God forbids. If pronesse and inclination to euill bee in man and wo∣man by nature; why then doth God giue a Law against it: for being naturall, it seemes not to be euill, or at least it cannot be helped. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; pronesse and inclination in man or wo∣man to euill, is now naturall, and cannot bee helped, be∣cause man is now fallen from the state of innocencie, in which hee was created: but it was not so before the fall of man; God made not man prone to euill by creation, but man brought that pronesse on himselfe by his vo∣luntarie falling from the state of innocencie, in which hee was at the first created: and therefore though pro∣nesse to euill in man or woman bee naturall, yet it is e∣uill; and though it cannot bee helped, yet that is through mans owne voluntary fault, and God doth still iustly giue a law against it. The Anabaptists obiect against this, Psal. 51.5. Behold I was borne in iniquitie, and in sinne hath my mother conceiued me: Say they, Dauid there confesseth not his owne sinne, but his mothers sinne; that is, the curse or pu∣nishment for sinne layd on Eua, and so on Dauids Mother,
Gen. 3.16. Therefore it proues not that Dauid was concei∣ued and borne in sinne. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; Dauid had there no purpose, nor any cause or occasion to confesse the punishment for sinne layd on Eua, and so on his mother; but to acknowledge, and to set out his owne vilenesse, as appeares by the Context: which hee doth, not onely by confessing his actuall sinnes, but also the root of them, his naturall corruption: and ther∣fore that Exposition of theirs is contrary to the meaning of that place. tion.If Dauid here confesse his owne estate, then he confesseth to God, and desireth him in mercy to consider and behold him whereof he was made, as Psal. 103.14. of dust, weak flesh, vn∣able to resist the tempter, when the law came to him; through which weaknesse hee was ouercome in those horrible sinnes of Murther and Adultery. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; It cannot be that Dauid doth there desire God in mercy to consider him, as made of dust and weake flesh, vnable to resist the tempter: for that had been rather an extenuating and an excusing of his sinnes, then a set∣ting himselfe out as a grieuous sinner, which was the pur∣pose of Dauid. Againe, the matter of Dauids making is not there spoken of, but the corruption and sinne in which hee was framed and made; and so the manner of his making, that in his frame and making he was sinfull and corrupt, and the corruption of sinne did cleaue vnto him. biection.The soule of man comes from God, the matter of the body from the parents; and the soule comming from God is very good: therefore whole man is not conceiued & borne in sin. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; the soule of man as it comes from God, is very good; but being placed in the body, and ioyned with the bo∣dy, it is presently depriued of the image of God, as a iust pu∣nishment for the sin of Adam & all men in him, according to that order which God set downe in the Creation, that what∣soeuer
euill Adam procured, he should not onely bring it on himselfe, but on all his posteritie; and by vertue of that order,Rom. 5.12. the whole man both soule and body is conceiued and borne in sinne. Hence it is said, Genes. 5.3. that Adam begate a child in his owne likenesse. And that which is borne of a woman cannot bee cleane, Iob 25.4. Quest. What is the second thing the tenth Commandement forbids? Ans. This; the effects & fruits of the proness and inclinati∣on of our corrupt nature to euil, that are inward in the soule. Quest. What are those effects and fruits? Answ. Two especially. Quest. VVhat is the first of those? Answ. Euill and inordinate concupiscence, euery motion,Rom. 6.12. Galat. 5.17. Coloss. 3.5. euen the first motion comming from the rebellion of our na∣ture, whereby we are stirred vp to euill, and doe with delight think any thing contrary to the loue of God or man, though we neuer giue consent of will to commit that euill, as fond wishing and woulding, delightfull remembrances, and medi∣tations of euill, Rom. 7.7. called the lusting of the flesh. In our nature now corrupt, the motion, appetite, or de∣sire to such things as tend to the conseruation of nature is not euill, but such is concupiscence or appetite after meat, and drinke, and the like: therefore concupiscence is not e∣uill and a sinne. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; Motions and appetites after meat and drink, and such like, tending to the conseruation of nature, are not euill of themselues, and as they be naturall motions; for they were in Christ, he was hungry and thirstie: but if they be immoderate and exceed a iust measure, they are euill. Againe, there be other concupiscences and desires besides these, as after another mans house, or wife, or the like, which are euill, and cannot be so excused. The Papists obiect Jam. 1.15. When lust or concupiscence hath conceiued, it brings forth sinne: and therefore lust or concupiscence it selfe is no sinne, but onely brings forth sinne.
Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; it is no good consequent, Lust or concu∣piscence brings forth sinne; therefore it is no sinne: for one sinne may bring forth another: and we way rather thus con∣clude, lust or concupiscence brings forth sinne, therefore it is sinne: for the proper cause and mother of euill must needs be euill it selfe. n.That concupiscence remaining after Baptisme, is not pro∣perly sinne, nor forbidden by the Commandement of God, namely thus, sinne maketh guiltie before God of eternall death, and liable to condemnation: but the regenerate are not guiltie of eternall death: therefore concupiscence in them is no sinne. Quest. How is this to be answered? Answ. Thus; by this reason, there is no sinne at all in the regenerate: 1. for there is no condemnation at all to them, they be∣ing in Christ. Againe, neither concupiscence nor any other sinne shall condemne the regenerate; but that is not because concupi∣scence is no sin in them, but because both it and all other sins are pardoned to them in Christ, and so not imputed to them. on.Originall sinne is taken away in Baptisme: therfore con∣cupiscence is no sinne in the regenerate. Quest. How is this to bee answered? Answ. Thus; there be three things to be considered tou∣ching originall sinne:. 13.23.  2.1. the disagreement it hath with the Law of God, the corruption of nature, and the guiltinesse of it and the punishment due to it: in regard of the guiltinesse of Gods wrath, & also in regard of the punishment due to it, it is taken away in Baptisme; but in regard of the disagreement it hath with Gods Law, and the corruption of nature, it is not taken away, but still remaines in the regenerate, yet weakned through sanctification. Quest. Are delightfull remembrances of euill in the time of sleepe, as delightfull dreames of euill, sinfull and forbidden in this Commandement? Answ. As they be either fruits of corrupt nature, and do sa∣uour of nature, & be agreeable to mans corruption, which is
repugnant to Gods will, or be suggested by Satan,Deut. 23.10. Deut. 13.1.2. Ierem. 23.23. Ierem. 29.9.. they are euill and sinnefull, and forbidden in this Commandement: as vnchast dreames arising from the concupiscēce spoken of, Deut. 23.10. Such were the dreames of false Prophets, told by them, to draw men from the true worship of God to Apostacie. Delightfull remembrances of euill in the time of sleepe, as delightfull Dreames of euill cannot bee helped or a∣voyded. Quest: How then are they euill and sinfull? Answ. Though they cannot bee helped or auoyded,Eccles. 5.. yet comming from our owne disorder in diet, in speech or medi∣tations in the day time, they are fruites of our corruption: and the cause and occasion of them, is our selues; and so are euill and sinfull, as Eccles. 5.2. Quest. What is the second effect and fruite of the pronesse, and inclination of our owne corrupt nature to euill, that is inward in our soules? Answ. A suffering our selues to bee infected with those motions that Satan,1 Chron. 21.1.2. Luk. 22.3.4. Act. 5.3. Ephes. 4.23. or euill men doe put into our mindes, contrary to the true loue of God or man: by yeelding to them, and delighting in them, and hauing our hearts tickled with delight in them. A man cannot withstand the motions to euill, and con∣trary to the loue of God or man, that Satan brings to his minde, he hath no power of himselfe so to doe. Quest. Why then doth God giue to man a law to withstand them? Answ. Man had power to withstand them, in his state of innocencie, wherein God created him: but man lost that power by his voluntary fall from that state, and therefore God may and doth still giue and continue a law to man to withstand them. Question. Are motions to euill that are cast into the mindes of men by Satan, and presently reiected and compelled, sins or no? Answ. No, they are not, vnlesse they be receiued by some degree of delight or assent  for Christ was moued and temp∣ted by Satan, to infidelitie, to tempt God, to Idolatrie; yet
his holy heart receiued not those motions and temptations: 4.2. to 11.  14.30. so they neuer became his sinnes. Question. How shall we know the motions of euill that be in our mids, are put in our minds by Satan, and that they are not from the rebellion of our owne nature? Answ. Thus; if they be against the light of nature cor∣rupted, as for a man to kill his owne deare and louing Father or Mother, when there is no hope of gaine by it, or matter of displeasure to prouoke him thereunto: and so when blas∣phemous thoughts against God, come into our mindes furi∣ously and suddenly, like flashings of lightning, and wee can∣not imagine how or on what occasion wee should conceiue such thoughts;r. 12:7. and the more we striue to beate them away, the more they come vpon vs: and withall they are contriued subtilly, and artificially: then they are from Satan, and mes∣sengers of Satan. Question. How may the vglinesse of the euill motions in the soule of man, whether comming from the rebellion of our nature, or suggested by Satan, appeare? Answer. By two reasons. Quest. What is the first of those? eut. 27.26. lat. 3.10.Answ. This; because the curse of God, both in this life, and in death, and after death; euen the paines and torments of the damned in Hell, are due to the person of man or wo∣man, for them. Quest. What is the second reason by which the vglinesse of e∣uill motions in the soule of man, either comming from the rebel∣lion of our nature, or suggested by Satan and receiued, may ap∣peare? Answ. This; because such motions are the roote, and be∣ginning of all euill,Gen 6.5. in gesture, and word, and deede: for first there is a motion to euill in the soule, then delight in it, and from that comes consent of will, and after consent of will, followes execution of action. Now to the Affirmatiue part of this tenth Com∣mandement. Quest. What doth this tenth Commandement require? Answ. Two things in generall.
Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. Originall purity in all the powers and faculties of the soule,Deut. 6.5. Luk. 10.27. 1 Thess. 4.3. 1. Thess. 5 23. 1 Tim. 1.5. and an holy disposition and inclination of the soule, whereby a man or woman is at all times disposed to thinke well, and affect that which the Law of God requires, and is agreeable to the rule of perfect loue both of God and man. Quest. VVhat is the second thing the tenth Commandement requires? Answ. The inward effects and fruits of original puri∣ty in the soule, and of an holy disposition, and inclination of the soule. Quest. What are these inward effects and fruites? Answer. Two especially. Quest. What is the first of those? Answ. Good and holy motions of the minde and will,Psal 119.15.97.111. Rom. 7.22. 2 Cor. 10.5. Galat. 5.17. Ioh. epist. 3.2. whereby wee are stirred vp to good things, and to doe with delight, thinke and will, that which is agreeable to the true loue of God and man; is holy wishings and longings after good things: especially such things as concerne the glory of God, and the good of the soule; and delightfull remembran∣ces, and meditations of good things. Quest. What is the second inward effect, and fruite of origi∣nall purity in the soule, and of an holy disposition and inclination of the soule? Answ. A suppressing of euill thoughts, and motions to e∣uill, whether comming from the flesh within,Pro. 4.23. Mat. 16.22.23. or from Satan or euill men without: and a keeping them from taking any place in our mindes by the least assent to them, or the least deligt in them. Quest. What meanes are to be vsed to suppresse euill thoughts, and motions to euill, and to keepe them from taking place in our minds? Answ. Three especially. Quest. What is the first of those?Iob. 42.2. Psal. 94.11. Psal. 139.2.13. Act. 1 24. 1 Thess. 2.4. Answ. This; a rememberance and due consideration of this that God sees the verry secrets of our hearts, and that all our most hidden thoughts are naked and open to his sight.
Quest. What is the second meanes that is to be vsed to suppresse euill thoughts, and motions to euill, and to keepe them from taking place in our minds? Iob. 31.1. Psal. 119.37. Pro. 17.24.Ans. This; a couenanting with our outward senses, and a resoluing fully with our selues, by Gods grace that none of them shall be the instruments, the beginning or the occasion of sinne, in heart or life; and a carefull avoyding of all oc∣casions and obiects of lust. Quest. What is the third meanes that is to be vsed to suppresse euill thoughts and motions to euill, and to keepe them from taking place in our mindes? Answ. This; frequent, earnest and heartie prayer, often and earnest calling on the Lord,Psal. 119.36. Mat. 26, 41. Ephes. 6.18. that he would giue vs wise∣dome to discerne of the motions to euill, and strength against them: and that hee would incline our mindes and hearts to good things. Quest. Is it possible for any man or woman in this life, to keepe the morall law of God perfectly? Mat. 5.22.28.34. &c. Rom. 7.14.Answ. No: it is not possible, because the law of God is spirituall, and forbids not only the externall euill act, but al∣so the internall euill thought and motion to euill in the soule of man, though no consent of will be giuen to it; and it re∣quires absolute and perfect obedience to it, as well in the soule as in the body: and we are full of weakenesse and cor∣ruption and carnall in part, though we be regenerate. Quest. What vse then is there of the Morall Law of God, see∣ing it is impossible to keepe it perfectly in this life? Answ. It serues to teach vs the constant and vnchang∣able nature of it selfe,Leuit. 18.5. Ezech. 20.11. Rom. 3.20. 2 Cor. 3.7.9. Galat. 3.24. and to be the rule of our liues, and to shew vs the corruption of our natures and our weakenesse: and what we cannot doe, and so to humble vs, and to driue vs from it selfe, to seeke after grace and mercy in Christ. FINIS Decalogi.
